On ultrasound<b>, gallstones </b>are {{c1::echogenic::appearance}} with {{c2::posterior}} acoustic shadowing and are usually {{c3::mobile::mobile/stationary}}. Differential diagnosis of <b>echogenic material within the gallbladder</b> includes:<br><br><ol><li>{{c1::Gallstone}}: mobile, shadowing</li><li>{{c2::Gallbladder sludge}}: mobile, non-shadowing</li><li>{{c3::Gallbladder polyp}}: non-mobile, non-shadowing, often attached to gallbladder wall via stalk, may be vascular</li><li>{{c4::Hyperplastic cholecystoses}}: non-mobile, multiple polyps</li><li>{{c5::Porcelain gallbladder}}: echogenic wall, shadowing</li><li>{{c6::Adjacent bowel}}: echogenic wall, dirty shadowing</li></ol>				"<img src=""paste-724f1a901f2cc52b96e88ae0a32ab3af4a6c0ec6.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Gallstones and Cholecystitis	d49eb8c9-1842-4428-b69b-e89bd4653d12	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0131 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"

<b>{{c1::Courvoisier}} gallbladder</b> refers to a <u>markedly dilated gallbladder</u><b> </b>from <i>malignant obstruction</i> of the {{c2::<u>common bile duct</u>}}.	"originally described as being so large to be directly palpable on physical exam<br><br><b>Courvoisier sign&nbsp;or&nbsp;Courvoisier-Terrier sign</b>&nbsp;states that in a patient with&nbsp;painless jaundice&nbsp;and an&nbsp;enlarged gallbladder&nbsp;(or right upper quadrant mass),<b>&nbsp;the cause is unlikely&nbsp;to be&nbsp;gallstones&nbsp;and therefore presumes the cause to be an obstructing&nbsp;pancreatic&nbsp;or&nbsp;biliary neoplasm&nbsp;</b>until proven otherwise (Radiopaedia)<br><br>Example: Enlarged gallbladder (15cm) with a hypodense pancreatic head lesion seen in the same slice<br><img src=""7731d621d344d29d053fbc11891c046e.webp""><br>Case courtesy of Chris O'Donnell, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 19227<br><img src=""paste-b3e35ececb4cc5d30c644297d953f7d53b9c15da.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-c803fe0736f815ea2eb1976e59e2334410a9bd8d.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Gallstones and Cholecystitis	152dc37b-5d5a-48ce-8a42-57b8421924e3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0135 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
A&nbsp;<u>markedly dilated gallbladder</u><b>&nbsp;</b><i>without acute cholecystitis</i> implies {{c1::<u>chronic</u>::acute/chronic}}<u> obstruction</u> of either the {{c2::cystic}} duct <i>(when seen in isolation)</i> or the {{c3::common bile}} duct <i>(when seen in combination with intrahepatic biliary dilation)</i>.	"<b>Courvoisier sign&nbsp;or&nbsp;Courvoisier-Terrier sign</b>&nbsp;states that in a patient with&nbsp;painless jaundice&nbsp;and an&nbsp;enlarged gallbladder&nbsp;(or right upper quadrant mass),<b> the cause is unlikely&nbsp;to be&nbsp;gallstones&nbsp;and therefore presumes the cause to be an obstructing&nbsp;pancreatic&nbsp;or&nbsp;biliary neoplasm&nbsp;</b>until proven otherwise (Radiopaedia)<br><br>Example: Enlarged gallbladder (15cm) with a hypodense pancreatic head lesion seen in the same slice<br><img src=""7731d621d344d29d053fbc11891c046e.webp""><br>Case courtesy of Chris O'Donnell, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 19227"			"<img src=""paste-c803fe0736f815ea2eb1976e59e2334410a9bd8d.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Gallstones and Cholecystitis	7eddddc3-be50-463d-baad-4b41cd5f0444	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0135 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c2::Hyperplastic cholecystoses}}</b>&nbsp;are a spectrum of non-neoplastic proliferative disorders caused by {{c1::deposition of cholesterol-laden macrophages::pathology}} within the gallbladder wall.	"Includes&nbsp;<b>adenomyomatosis&nbsp;</b>and&nbsp;<b>cholesterolosis&nbsp;<br><img src=""95950510c49e68d889be1da538d43899.webp""><br><img src=""paste-65cceba9be3f297531a5ee37714ce70a4f03d99d.jpg"" width=""722""></b>"			"<img src=""paste-c803fe0736f815ea2eb1976e59e2334410a9bd8d.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hyperplastic Cholecystoses	c52beb17-3742-46fe-bb5c-2c07e1fcbfa8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0135 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Hyperplastic cholecystoses</b>&nbsp;are a spectrum of non-neoplastic proliferative disorders that includes abnormalities of the {{c1::gallbladder wall::structure}} <i>(adenomyomatosis and strawberry gallbladder)</i> to extension into the&nbsp;{{c2::lumen}} <i>(polyps)</i>.	"Includes&nbsp;<b>adenomyomatosis</b> (intraluminal)&nbsp;and&nbsp;<b>cholesterolosis </b>(within the gallbladder wall)<br><br><img src=""95950510c49e68d889be1da538d43899.webp""><br><br><b>Strawberry gallbladder</b> on US and path correlate (different patients):<br><img src=""0203383d1c492584a53994fdf276ff70.webp""><img src=""9b8cbca6f17addbd992aafdab5cf605d.webp""><br>The fundus of the gallbladder is filled with heterogeneous, echogenic material. d732a2b333c740f8881c857ce68a0718-ao-6	MRCP Anatomy	"<img src=""tmp3dxm5e9f.jpg"">"						"<img src=""d732a2b333c740f8881c857ce68a0718-ao-6-Q.svg"">"	"<img src=""d732a2b333c740f8881c857ce68a0718-ao-6-A.svg"">"	"<img src=""d732a2b333c740f8881c857ce68a0718-ao-O.svg"">"	a8581383-4a52-4127-b827-c506324e990b		"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>MRCP</b> utilizes heavily T{{c1::2}}-weighted sequences that increase contrast between <u>hyperintense stationary fluid</u><b> </b>and surrounding structures.	"<img src=""paste-05cd27a2f01acd5a05ca20334e7fd38e79c13993.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-26fc195c91b7244c06aa5ccea1af0e155bc34969.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Magnetic Resonance Cholangiopancreatography (MRCP)	16def63c-71b5-4005-bff8-744a84ea22eb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
Sequences with <b>intermediate </b>T2-weighted (TE {{c1::80-100}} ms) are best suited for visualization of the biliary ductal system and surrounding tissue.	"<img src=""paste-d87bf05a3e75968bd4b1285fb7cd484ab1dc4cbb.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-26fc195c91b7244c06aa5ccea1af0e155bc34969.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Magnetic Resonance Cholangiopancreatography (MRCP)	8c6d6c35-cc81-4a08-99c3-6d8cad15a8b5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::(FSE) Fast spin echo}}</b> sequences are<b> </b>most commonly used for {{c2::MRCP::study}} acquisition.				"<img src=""paste-26fc195c91b7244c06aa5ccea1af0e155bc34969.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Magnetic Resonance Cholangiopancreatography (MRCP)	cd5e37c3-7b75-4206-9e8c-c3f01fb32675	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Advantages </b>of <b>MRCP </b>over ERCP include:<br><br><ol><li>{{c1::Noninvasive::invasive/noninvasive}}</li><li>{{c2::Does <u>not</u>::does/does not}} require sedation</li><li>{{c3::Can::can/cannot}} visualize surrounding anatomy</li></ol>	"<img src=""paste-0f14380e371a00192c183127d23ca37aee3b8d18.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-26fc195c91b7244c06aa5ccea1af0e155bc34969.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Magnetic Resonance Cholangiopancreatography (MRCP)	426fb379-361e-41b6-bc82-9f48940e64bf	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>MRCP</b> <u>cannot</u> simultaneously {{c1::diagnose}} and {{c2::treat}}.	"whereas ERCP can do both<br><br><img src=""paste-fac6715f92d8d55dd65f8d2fe329ae712fd10fee.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-26fc195c91b7244c06aa5ccea1af0e155bc34969.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Magnetic Resonance Cholangiopancreatography (MRCP)	5f370986-9837-468f-af19-623532c31b13	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0138 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Contrast-enhanced MRCP</b> can be performed with fat-saturated T{{c2::1}}-weighted imaging after injection of gadolinium contrast agents that have <u>biliary excretion</u> like <b>{{c1::gadoxetic acid disodium (Eovist)}}</b>. Choledochal cysts:<br><br>Type I: {{c1::fusiform common bile duct dilation}}<br>Type II: {{c2::extrahepatic saccular dilation}}<br>Type III: {{c3::dilation of intraduodenal bile duct}}<br>Type IVA: {{c4::intra- and extrahepatic dilation (multiple)}}<br>Type IVB: {{c5::extrahepatic dilation only (multiple)}}<br>Type V: {{c6::intrahepatic dilation}}	"<img src=""paste-3b49aa25dcf978fcfb077dfdea441cec759a3bd8.jpg"">&nbsp;<img src=""0725d60641e8c656bb77f0353a024200.webp"">"			"<img src=""paste-e32bf4bfc87d01bef8276338bf52b98de32eda82.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Choledochal Cysts	a93373c6-be21-444f-98a5-65008eadf039	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0139 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
Most <b>{{c3::choledochal cysts}} </b>are diagnosed during {{c1::childhood}} presenting with {{c2::nonspecific abdominal}} pain or found incidentally. <b>Choledochal cysts </b>are often {{c1::resected::treatment}} due to increased {{c1::<u>cholangiocarcinoma</u>::pathologic}} risk, which can be as high as 25%.				"<img src=""paste-e32bf4bfc87d01bef8276338bf52b98de32eda82.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Choledochal Cysts	6484f56d-ff2f-44be-ab47-c73bfc7de63e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0139 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::03_Biliary_imaging Core_Radiology_2E"
In contrast to <i>biliary hamartomas</i>, <b>choledochal cysts&nbsp;</b>{{c1::do::do/do not}} communicate with the biliary tree. <b>{{c1::Pancreas divisum}}</b> is the<b> </b><u>most common</u> congenital pancreatic ductal anomaly caused by failure of fusion of the {{c2::<u>ventral</u>}} and {{c2::<u>dorsal</u>}}<u> pancreatic ducts</u>. In <b>{{c1::pancreas divisum}}</b>, the {{c2::duct of Wirsung}} <u>only</u> drains the ventral portion of the pancreas. <b>{{c2::Pancreas divisum}}</b> increases the risk for {{c1::<u>pancreatitis</u>::complication}} due to inability of the {{c3::minor}} papilla to adequately drain the majority of the pancreatic parenchyma. Treatment<b> </b>of <b>pancreas divisum</b> is {{c1::sphincterotomy::surgery}} or {{c2::stenting::procedure}}. <b>{{c1::Annular pancreas}} </b>is a rare congenital anomaly where a portion of the pancreas encircles the {{c2::duodenum}}, secondary to<b> </b><u>incomplete rotation</u><b> </b>of the {{c3::ventral}} pancreatic bud. In {{c1::neonates::demographic}}, {{c2::<b>annular pancreas</b>::congenital pancreatic malformation}} presents with {{c3::<u>duodenal</u>}}<u> obstruction</u> and is in the <i>differential</i><b> </b>for the {{c4::<u>double bubble</u>}}<u> sign</u>. In <b>{{c1::common channel syndrome}}</b> (aka {{c2::pancreaticobiliary maljunction}}), a <u>thin septum</u> separating the {{c3::<u>common bile</u>}}<u> duct</u> and {{c4::<u>duct of Wirsung</u> (main pancreatic)}} duct is <i>absent</i>, allowing for <u>reflux</u> between the two systems. <b>Pancreatitis </b>is<b>&nbsp;</b>inflammation of the pancreas, which may result in <u>premature activation of </u>{{c1::<u>enzymes</u>}} and resultant {{c2::<u>autodigestion</u>}} of the parenchyma.				"<img src=""paste-61e51d03abfa635635042376beccf0e128012e12.jpg""><img src=""paste-5856eaacad6db262c09e8f5db1ab208e0de057f2.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	8ab5f88a-d259-4bc7-82de-2ce4d763a8cc	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0149 #Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0150 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Pancreatitis </b>ranges in severity from {{c1::mild self-limited}} disease to {{c2::necrotizing}} infection resulting in multiorgan failure and death.				"<img src=""paste-61e51d03abfa635635042376beccf0e128012e12.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	6b29e6ba-908a-435c-ba1c-da17677370e2	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0150 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Ultrasound::Modality}} is useful in the&nbsp;<u>initial evaluation</u><b>&nbsp;</b>of clinically suspected <b>acute pancreatitis</b> to evaluate for {{c2::gallstones::etiology}}, {{c3::choledocholithiasis::etiology}} or {{c4::biliary obstruction::etiology}}.				"<img src=""paste-61e51d03abfa635635042376beccf0e128012e12.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	42f68e9e-763e-4b03-9134-6d3c6e742525	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0150 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Ultrasound::Modality}} has limited utility in evaluating <b>complications of pancreatitis </b>such as {{c2::pancreatic necrosis}} or {{c3::peripancreatic fluid collections}}.				"<img src=""paste-61e51d03abfa635635042376beccf0e128012e12.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	6dc47aee-1d30-4921-8a2b-96c5fca9d416	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0150 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"
Imaging of <b>pancreatitis</b> is ideally performed in the pancreatic phase ({{c1::late arterial}}; about {{c2::40}} seconds after contrast injection when parenchyma is maximally enhancing), which is the optimal time to detect {{c3::necrosis}} (areas of decreased enhancement). {{c1::CT}} imaging may be helpful when:<br><br><ol><li>The clinical presentation is {{c2::equivocal}} for pancreatitis</li><li>A patient is critically ill or worsening over time</li><li>To assess {{c3::severity}} or {{c4::complications}}</li><li>Guide treatment</li></ol>	Diagnosis is made when 2 out of 3 criteria are met:<br><br><ol><li><u>Symptoms</u> consistent with pancreatitis (e.g. epigastric pain)</li><li>Elevation of serum <u>amylase</u> or <u>lipase</u> (to 3 times normal level)</li><li><u>Radiological features</u> consistent with pancreatitis (e.g. CT or MRI)</li></ol>			"<img src=""paste-61e51d03abfa635635042376beccf0e128012e12.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	0cca46c7-43ee-49a8-9083-4f987d7ffa02	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0150 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"
CT imaging {{c1::is <u>not</u>::is/is not}} indicated in patients with clinical diagnosis of <b><i>mild</i> acute pancreatitis</b>. {{c1::CT}} imaging may be <i>negative</i><b> </b>or show <u>mildly edematous pancreas</u> in a case of <b><i>mild</i> acute pancreatitis</b>. <u>Extra-pancreatic</u> complications of <b>pancreatitis</b>:<br><br><ol><li><b>Perihilar renal inflammation</b>, may lead to {{c1::<u>venous compression</u>}} or {{c2::<u>thrombosis</u>}}</li><li><b>Bowel involvement</b>, may see <u>ileus</u> or even <u>fistula</u> often to the {{c3::transverse colon::segment}} or {{c4::duodenum::segment}}</li></ol>				"<img src=""paste-370007e2c31874a4734807cbab73febe735c6c03.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Pancreatitis	b1e2b81f-44d7-46eb-8386-252fd54bc6aa	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0151 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::04_Pancreas Core_Radiology_2E"

<b>Chronic pancreatitis</b> is <i>most commonly</i> due to {{c1::long-term <u>alcohol abuse</u>}} and causes {{c2::<u>irreversible</u>::reversible/irreversible}} damage. In<b> ulcerative colitis</b>, a {{c1::collar-button}} ulcer is nonspecific but represents {{c2::<u>submucosal extension</u>}} of mucosal ulceration. {{c1::CT colonography}} is increasingly being used as a non-invasive alternative to colonoscopy for <b>colon cancer screening</b>.	"<img src=""paste-3a7506334683dc57a36507259b81d98bb14e1cf3.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c0b03c01f3c56c4b4126e7abe66ddd92.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colorectal Carcinoma	507c5505-63a5-4630-9a03-7b9a92801314	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0220 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
Patients with <b>colon cancer</b> may be asymptomatic at diagnosis by CT&nbsp;colonography, but may present with imaging findings of {{c1::obstruction}} or {{c1::perforation}}.	"<img src=""paste-103f80a9c6b8a82e400b00f11becfb3b736b5c81.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c0b03c01f3c56c4b4126e7abe66ddd92.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colorectal Carcinoma	7c809be7-c9d2-44d8-a422-1fee82ffec52	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0220 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::CT}} is the modality most often used for <u>staging</u> of <b>colorectal carcinoma</b>.	"<img src=""paste-103f80a9c6b8a82e400b00f11becfb3b736b5c81.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c0b03c01f3c56c4b4126e7abe66ddd92.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colorectal Carcinoma	2a186d13-187c-479d-91a4-e9ee67612592	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0220 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
Typical features of <b>colorectal&nbsp;carcinomas</b> on CT/MRI:<br><br>{{c1::Soft tissue}} density&nbsp;masses that may {{c1::narrow}} the bowel lumen and can cause {{c2::ulceration}} when they grow.	"<img src=""paste-28be5fc6540a812702f62926bee9c721b94f7c46.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c0b03c01f3c56c4b4126e7abe66ddd92.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colorectal Carcinoma	0d4f7c29-dcb0-4915-9622-3bd089ebd841	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0220 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
MRI is typically used in <b>colorectal&nbsp;carcinomas</b>&nbsp;for {{c1::locoregional staging::purpose}}.	"<img src=""paste-28be5fc6540a812702f62926bee9c721b94f7c46.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c0b03c01f3c56c4b4126e7abe66ddd92.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colorectal Carcinoma	f96dc021-e699-4f16-b20b-060a8e9cd0f2	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0220 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Familial adenomatous polyposis (FAP)}}</b> is an <u>autosomal dominant</u>&nbsp;syndrome with innumerable premalignant <i>adenomatous</i>&nbsp;polyps in the <u>colon</u>*.&nbsp;	"*Small bowel and Gastric polyps may also be present.<br><br><img src=""paste-28f452b6301e7adf2f6b593c8b8457d81e8191a5.jpg"">"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	1c9ff063-efa2-472c-8f94-38e76d13249e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Turcot}} syndrome</b> is another variant of familial adenomatous polyposis&nbsp;(FAP) in which&nbsp;patients also have&nbsp;{{c2::CNS tumors (gliomas and medulloblastomas)}}.	"<img src=""paste-28f452b6301e7adf2f6b593c8b8457d81e8191a5.jpg"">"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	6749673e-0cbc-4609-80b3-6c847b9e13a4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
"<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">Yellow&nbsp;⇉</span>: Fluid-filled colon with innumerable {{c2::polypoid enhancing lesions::⇉}}&nbsp;<br><br>Diagnosis:<b>&nbsp;{{c1::(FAP) Familial adenomatous polyposis}}</b><br><br><img src=""paste-87361e5fe52f830d0a2de87bc2a8326f15cafdc1.jpg"">"	"<img src=""paste-28f452b6301e7adf2f6b593c8b8457d81e8191a5.jpg"">"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	b8bc50c4-1978-4296-bb03-f5fc6d61dd6f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Hereditary nonpolyposis colon cancer (HNPCC) syndrome (aka Lynch syndrome)}}</b> is an <u>autosomal dominant</u>&nbsp;polyposis syndrome caused by DNA {{c2::mismatch repair}}.	"<img src=""paste-50100e21c277bdaab1e9a72afe8318e34ef0e923.jpg"">"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	424e7220-9544-4d75-9c07-22e9ee5cde09	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Peutz-Jeghers}}</b>&nbsp;is an <u>autosomal dominant</u>&nbsp;syndrome that features {{c3::<i>hamartomatous&nbsp;pedunculated</i>::type}} polyps in the {{c2::<u>small</u>}}<u> bowel</u>.&nbsp;	"<img src=""paste-50100e21c277bdaab1e9a72afe8318e34ef0e923.jpg""><br><br>The polyps&nbsp;most commonly involve the small intestine (predominantly the jejunum), but also colon and stomach; mouth and oesophagus are spared.<br><div>These polyps are non-neoplastic&nbsp;<a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/articles/hamartoma"">hamartomas</a>&nbsp;due to the proliferation of all three layers of the mucosa, which have a <u>characteristic feature of a smooth muscle core continuous with muscularis mucosa in a tree-like branching pattern</u>. This distinguishes them from the hamartomatous polyps of&nbsp;<a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/articles/cronkhite-canada-syndrome-1"">Cronkhite-Canada syndrome</a>,&nbsp;<a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/articles/juvenile-polyposis-syndrome"">juvenile polyposis</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/articles/cowden-syndrome"">Cowden disease</a>.</div>Patients are at increased risk of GI tract adenocarcinoma, <u>although the polyps themselves are not premalignant</u>. Theres also increased risk of other malignancies, including breast, lung, testicular and gynaecologic malignancies.<br><br>*Radiopaedia"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	14fcb733-1496-466c-a66f-19d15c864da0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Cowden}} syndrome</b> is an <u>autosomal dominant</u> syndrome of multiple <i>hamartomatous</i> polyps usually&nbsp;found in the skin, external mucous membranes, and in the GI tract.	"<img src=""paste-60782a6683fd6d9aaf4bd451f8d9d5deac06bbeb.jpg"">"			"<img src=""e13ab8c49aeb46bd78bb9e3178f52163.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	d07fc13b-4453-49c0-a276-cd9534024b38	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0221 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Cronkhite-Canada}}&nbsp;is a&nbsp;<u>non-inherited disorder</u> consisting of <i>hamartomatous</i> polyps <u>throughout the GI tract</u>.	"whereas familial Peutz-Jeghers syndrome is an autosomal dominant disorder that usually involves small bowel<br><br><img src=""paste-5249e369ba76f081cd79220c757263e7e0bf1036.jpg"">"			"<img src=""paste-5249e369ba76f081cd79220c757263e7e0bf1036.jpg"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Polyposis Syndromes Affecting the Bowel	d7740275-88c9-41ba-9904-f8a468e5b4b5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Submucosal fat}} deposition in <b>ulcerative colitis </b>(and in <b>Crohn’s</b>)&nbsp;suggests <u>chronic disease</u>.	"<img alt=""EPOS&amp;trade;"" src=""872233""><img src=""paste-1a503a5c4cecb9bb2d32a4892eee5ef191764cce.jpg"">"			"<img src=""c4f7074d7a3b8b5d690959730eed987e.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colitis	15d41c29-16ea-4ac7-a0c7-773d6e90109e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0216 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
In the setting of <b>ischemic colitis</b>, if <u>chronic arterial stenosis</u> is suspected, evaluate for {{c1::atherosclerosis::pathology}} of the {{c1::mesenteric vessels::structures}}.&nbsp;	"<img src=""paste-809364ffc3c11d47ef69b6545a39eb5e2096a5be.jpg"">"			"<img src=""020e37ca4c8147115268c4fb037677a4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Colitis	0eb925ab-77b4-436c-8ea2-51ae68e76b39	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0214 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::09_Large_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Colonoscopy}} is <i>contraindicated</i> in patients with suspected&nbsp;<b>toxic megacolon</b> due to risk of as colonic&nbsp;<u>perforation</u>. <b>Uncomplicated diverticulitis </b>does not include signs of {{c1::bowel perforation}}. {{c1::Follow-up CT::Tests}} or {{c1::colonoscopy}} may be recommended to distinguish between the extensive {{c2::colonic wall thickening::finding}} seen in both&nbsp;<u>acute diverticulitis</u> and <u>colon cancer</u>. <div><u>Couinaud Classification</u><br></div><br><div><b></b>Mnemonic for remembering the segments:</div><div>&nbsp; <br>{{c1::Superior}} segments, from left to right: 2, 4, 8, 7, 1 (caudate). 2 doubled is 4; 4 doubled is 8; 8 minus 1 is 7.<br><div>{{c1::Inferior}} segments, from left to right: 3, 4, 5, 6.<br></div></div>	"<img src=""46109098802551fc7805c2c4892fe623.webp"">"			"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	16ceedc0-6b2f-44a5-81e4-9d1e322821ea	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><u>Couinaud Classification</u><br></div><br><div>Small {{c1::hepatic vein tributaries::structures}} mark the peripheral margins of each segment.<br><b></b></div>				"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	dd7274fe-03de-4f71-9d95-5d9cdd713274	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The <b>caudate lobe</b> drains to the {{c1::IVC::vein}}, not into the hepatic veins.<br></div><div><b></b></div>				"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	8fd98aa4-d807-4464-8fb8-c89595d528dd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>&nbsp;The <b>{{c1::caudate}} lobe</b> is often not affected in early cirrhosis.&nbsp;</div><br><div>This leads to&nbsp;{{c2::compensatory hypertrophy::change}} of the {{c1::caudate}} lobe, which is a typical morphologic change of<br></div><div>early cirrhosis.<br><b></b></div>	"<span>The <u>direct drainage to the IVC s</u></span><span><u>pares the caudate</u><b> </b>from increased venous pressures due to portal hypertension<br></span><br><div>Caudate-right lobe ratio (C/RL) is taken at an axial slice&nbsp;<b>immediately below the bifurcation of the main portal vein</b>, 3 lines are drawn as below:<br></div><br><div><img src=""667b9c9ab38e1c413a36b73cb216609a.webp""><br></div><div><ul><li><div><b>line 1:&nbsp;</b>parasagittal line drawn through the right lateral border of the main portal vein</div></li><li><div><b>line 2:</b>&nbsp;parasagittal line drawn through the left lateral border of the caudate lobe</div></li><li><div><b>line 3:</b>&nbsp;line orthogonal to lines 1 and 2 midway between the main portal vein and the inferior vena cava extended to the right liver edge</div></li><li><div><b>caudate measurement (C):</b>&nbsp;along line 3, between lines 1 and 2</div></li><li><div><b>right lobe measurement (RL):</b>&nbsp;along line 3, from right liver edge to line 1</div></li><li><div><b>caudate-right lobe ratio:</b>&nbsp;C/RL</div></li></ul><div>Interpretation<ul><li><div>C/RL &lt;0.6 = normal (does not exclude cirrhosis)&nbsp;</div></li><li><div>C/RL 0.6-0.65 = borderline</div></li><li><div>C/RL &gt;0.65 = 96% likely to be cirrhotic</div></li><li><div>C/RL &gt;0.73 = 99% likely to be cirrhotic</div></li></ul></div></div>"			"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	e5541761-3171-4c44-9cf8-c532da9af9b7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Compensatory hypertrophy</u> of the {{c1::caudate}} lobe may preserve liver function in <b>Budd-Chiari syndrome</b>.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Direct venous drainage to the IVC allows the caudate lobe to <u>bypass the increased hepatic</u></div><div><u>venous pressures</u> seen in Budd-Chiari syndrome.&nbsp;</div>			"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	6bf291bb-fa39-4b3c-804e-bd95a09a44d1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>The <b>{{c1::papillary}} process</b> is a medial projection of the {{c2::<u>caudate</u>}}<u> lobe</u> and can be mistaken for <i>lymphadenopathy</i> or even a <i>mass</i> as it may appear separate from the medial process on a single axial slice.<br></div><br><div><img src=""57c87b83af95c10ead789c449d90f54a.webp""><br></div><div></div>"	"<div>elongated papillary process of the caudate lobe (purple)<br></div><br><div>AKA the medial process of the caudate lobe (the lateral process is contiguous with the right liver lobe and what we refer to as the ""caudate"" lobe when it is really the lateral process of the caudate lobe)<br></div><br><div>Radiopaedia</div>"			"<img src=""2ed565013d36f7154614842b95664ac4.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Anatomy	a8e03ae7-26f0-4229-bded-0bfe61be4472	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0097 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>A “routine” contrast-enhanced abdominal CT is acquired in the <b>{{c1::portal venous}} phase </b>of enhancement, obtained {{c2::70}} seconds following intravenous contrast administration.</div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<img src=""90fc4e6fa0390d5894d81ade421d60a5.webp""><br><img src=""9977b45f97807260eaea7eb7383502a2.webp""><br><a href=""https://radiologyassistant.nl/more/ct-protocols/ct-contrast-injection-and-protocols"">The Radiology Assistant : CT contrast injection and protocols</a>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	e0f624c9-10c8-4433-b1dd-692a7d4b3380	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>In the <b>portal venous phase</b>, the&nbsp;liver should be homogeneously enhancing, allowing detection of attenuation alterations and/or morphologic changes of {{c1::<u>diffuse</u>}}<u> liver disease</u>, such as hepatic <u>steatosis</u> and <u>cirrhosis</u>.&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	a137df70-0da4-4d00-9b08-e4d2258a04d8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>As most <b>metastatic tumors</b> are <u>not hypervascular</u> (with a few notable exceptions), liver metastases can also generally be detected on the <b>portal venous phase</b> as {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>attenuating</u> masses.&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Of note, <u>some breast cancers may rarely be <b>isoattenuating</b></u> on the portal venous phase and may be <u>more conspicuous on unenhanced CT.</u><br></div>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	e0e38e0f-5ae2-4e47-a9b9-ccc8d89ad085	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>In the <b>portal venous phase</b>, contrast should be seen in&nbsp;{{c1::<u>both</u> the portal and hepatic veins::<i>only</i> the portal veins, or <i>both</i> the portal and hepatic veins}}.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	1bddb60d-e141-459c-8b62-4decf5872bd7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>Most benign and malignant <b>primary liver masse</b>s are <u>hypervascular</u> and thus are most conspicuous in the <b>{{c1::late arterial}} phase</b> of enhancement (~45 seconds).&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""90fc4e6fa0390d5894d81ade421d60a5.webp"" style=""text-align: start;""><br style=""text-align: start;""><img src=""9977b45f97807260eaea7eb7383502a2.webp"" style=""text-align: start;""><br style=""text-align: start;""><a href=""https://radiologyassistant.nl/more/ct-protocols/ct-contrast-injection-and-protocols"" style=""text-align: start;"">The Radiology Assistant : CT contrast injection and protocols</a><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	ef21a408-15df-477d-be5a-7d765ffa36dc	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>If the patient has a <u>known hypervascular primary malignancy</u>, both a <b>{{c1::late arterial}} phase</b> and <b>{{c1::portal venous}} phase</b> may be obtained for metastatic workup and restaging.&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	699b833b-11f7-4555-b626-12e10ca44b8d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver CT</u><br></div><br><div>If the patient has a <u>suspected primary liver mass</u> (such as hemangioma, focal nodular hyperplasia, hepatocellular carcinoma), a multiphase CT or MRI may be obtained, usually including a:</div><br><div><ul><li>{{c1::noncontrast}} phase</li><li>{{c1::arterial}} phase</li><li>{{c1::portal venous}} phase&nbsp;</li><li>{{c1::delayed}} phase</li></ul></div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""90fc4e6fa0390d5894d81ade421d60a5.webp""><br><img src=""9977b45f97807260eaea7eb7383502a2.webp""><br><a href=""https://radiologyassistant.nl/more/ct-protocols/ct-contrast-injection-and-protocols"">The Radiology Assistant : CT contrast injection and protocols</a><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	9895394a-8fee-4ef6-a2c2-2036f5354ce0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div>Compared to CT, MRI of the liver has superior {{c1::lesion}}-to-{{c1::liver}} contrast.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	dfd05cf1-5483-4d05-b080-677599041018	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>In- and out-of-phase gradient imaging</b> allows for detection of {{c1::<u>intracytoplasmic lipid</u>}}, which is seen in hepatic steatosis and may be seen within certain masses, including <u>hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC)</u> and <u>adenomas</u>.&nbsp;</div><br><div><b>{{c2::(DWI) Diffusion-weighted}}</b> imaging is useful for detection of <u>metastatic</u> lesions.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	ef452228-a0d7-46b5-9556-23814186f656	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::Combined extracellular/hepatobiliary::Type of}} contrast agents </b>pass through the intravascular system and interstitium similarly to CT contrast, <u>but are partially excreted through the biliary system</u>.&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""9711995975c80642c468667c812f7743.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	3d6456df-47ea-4278-8ebf-021421f9a420	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::MultiHance (Gadobenate dimeglumine)}}&nbsp;</b>is a <u>combined extracellular/hepatobiliary contrast agent</u> that requires a 1 hour delay due to low uptake into the liver and is now mainly used in pelvic, cardiac, and MSK imaging.</div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""9711995975c80642c468667c812f7743.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	124abe99-f1fc-4418-abe4-b15b0b51bce2	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::Gadoxetic acid disodium (Eovist)}}&nbsp;</b>is a <u>combined extracellular/hepatobiliary contrast agent</u> that is taken up by the liver in the delayed phase and is used to differentiate:</div><br><div><ol><li>{{c2::FNH::Benign tumor}} versus {{c2::adenoma::benign tumor}}</li><li>{{c3::Metastasis::Type of malignant tumor}} versus {{c3::primary::other type}}</li></ol></div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div>FNH is iso-to-hyperintense (tends to retain due to <u>malformed biliary ducts</u>)</div><br><div><img src=""9711995975c80642c468667c812f7743.webp""><br></div><br><div>AKA Primovist in EU / Australia / New Zealand<br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	8d6eb5cd-0599-46a6-af5c-12b1de8bdc8c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::Ferumoxides or ferumoxytol::Contrast agent}}&nbsp;</b>particles are trapped in Kupffer cells and reduce T2 relaxivity, making the liver or spleen <u>dark</u> on T2.</div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""9711995975c80642c468667c812f7743.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	8fc6977d-9cc5-42c8-9adf-6241355e08b1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver MRI</u><br></div><br><div><b>Ferumoxides or ferumoxytol&nbsp;</b>particles are used as an adjunct for detection of&nbsp;{{c2::HCC}}.</div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><img src=""9711995975c80642c468667c812f7743.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""f331c49a4e4ee50825334fbf779ad425.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	21fad07b-1d8b-4fce-aff3-0bee541c0162	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0098 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver Ultrasound</u><br></div><br><div>Ultrasound of the liver is often used to evaluate patients with abnormal LFTs, as it can identify {{c1::biliary::structure}} pathology and diffuse {{c1::parenchymal::tissue}} processes.&nbsp;<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	14ebd14f-386b-4ebe-b6b3-41f1530bd3d9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver Ultrasound</u><br></div><br><div>{{c1::Ultrasound::Modality}} is commonly used as a&nbsp;<u>screening</u>&nbsp;tool for <b>HCC</b> in high-risk patients given its relatively low cost and lack of ionizing radiation.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<div><u>Characterization</u> of hepatic masses, however, requires further workup&nbsp;with cross-sectional imaging.&nbsp;<br></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	794e45db-9f50-4a4b-8c39-af07018505f5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Liver Ultrasound</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c2::Hepatic Doppler}} ultrasound </b>is a valuable tool for determining <u>abnormal blood flow</u> to, within, or from the liver and can also be utilized to evaluate <u>transplants</u> and {{c1::<u>TIPS</u>::IR procedure}}.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Imaging of the Liver	a48ab29c-d6c2-490c-b2ff-2de6d7e26027	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>(NAFLD) Nonalcoholic fatty liver disease / (MASLD) metabolic dysfunction-associated steatotic liver disease</b> can be divided into {{c1::<u>steatosis</u>::pathologic change}} and {{c1::steatosis with associated inflammatory activity (<u>steatohepatitis</u>)::pathologic change}}.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Overall, &gt;25% of the population is afflicted with NAFLD and approximately 5% have steatohepatitis.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Ultimately, steatohepatitis may progress to cirrhosis.<br></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	706d51e1-07bb-49f4-a988-4897ecac2c33	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Overall, &gt;25% of the population is afflicted with {{c1::<b>MASLD</b>::diffuse liver disease}} and approximately<b> </b>5% have <u>steatohepatitis</u>.</div><br><div>Ultimately, steatohepatitis may progress to {{c2::<u>cirrhosis</u>}}.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	NAFLD renamed to <b>metabolic dysfunction-associated steatotic liver disease (MASLD)</b> in 2023			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	a7aee556-739e-4954-9bde-b80b921dc311	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Common patterns of <b>hepatic steatosis</b> include {{c1::diffuse::distributions}}, {{c1::focal}} <i>(commonly seen in the  gallbladder fossa and periportal spaces)</i>, {{c1::geographic}}, and {{c1::nodular}}. </div></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div>diffuse / focal:<br></div><div><img src=""https://liveratlas.org/media/cache/bb/dd/bbddbe407451c486ec71078336709752.jpg"">&nbsp;<img src=""https://liveratlas.org/media/cache/6d/37/6d379d94d1c2f9c561d3a899a69bece4.jpg""><br></div><div><i>&nbsp;</i><br></div><div><i>geographic:</i></div><div><img src=""https://liveratlas.org/media/cache/89/6d/896d34700a5763c493a1bca2edcbedd5.jpg"">&nbsp;<img src=""https://liveratlas.org/media/cache/a4/54/a454ffcd785d11aeaddc214c5d3aa6a4.jpg""><br></div><br><div>Nodular (or multifocal nodular)</div><div><img src=""5c8d60f13b47d179de5136406753c1c1.webp""><br></div><br><div><i>liveratlas.org/diagnosis/74 (UW), Radiopaedia</i><br></div>"			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	6a44c7dd-f9bf-46c7-a501-babecaa30e36	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>In <b>hepatic steatosis</b>, ultrasound shows a diffuse {{c1::increase::increase/decrease}} in hepatic echogenicity relative to the right kidney.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Normally, the liver and kidney should have the same echogenicity.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Hepatic steatosis also causes increased sound attenuation, leading to poor visualization of deeper structures.<br></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	287bb69c-f542-487b-9d55-d6adf423e72d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>In addition to an <u>increase in echogenicity</u>, <b>hepatic steatosis</b> also<br>causes <u>increased sound attenuation</u>, leading to {{c1::poor visualization of deeper structures}}.<br></div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	f0ad3c15-c5e0-4120-9e7a-775c459af285	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div>{{c1::Normal::Normal or steatotic}} liver<br></div><br><div><img src=""8443f58f365576d279f1305e9e883d7b.webp""><br></div></div><div><b></b></div>"	<div>Ultrasound of the liver and kidney shows the normal <u>isoechoic</u> appearance of liver relative to <u>renal cortex</u>.<br></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	c78df6d3-c3df-4ddb-be5e-2e739d05bb4b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div>{{c1::Steatotic::Normal or steatotic}} liver<br></div><br><div><img src=""2fbdae9a7394744e70963170830390ec.webp""><br></div></div><div><b></b></div>"	<div>Ultrasound shows <u>diffusely increased echogenicity</u> of the liver when compared to the renal cortex.<br></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	efb09c94-0b7e-4f75-a72c-9105dbb8fa56	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>In <b>hepatic steatosis</b>,&nbsp;CT<b>&nbsp;</b>shows <u>decreased attenuation</u> relative to the&nbsp;{{c1::spleen}}.</div></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	8ef5fb34-acaa-4eaf-9954-d91d89fd4187	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On unenhanced CT, the liver should be slightly {{c1::hyper}}attenuating relative to the spleen.&nbsp;<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	9854f96d-4faf-49b5-8881-3ba5a2a13fee	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The traditional teaching is that <b>steatosis </b>is present if the liver attenuates<b> ≥{{c1::10}} Hounsfield units (HU)</b> <u>less than</u> the spleen <i>on noncontrast CT</i>, although new work suggests that even a single HU of relative hypoattenuation compared to the spleen may represent hepatic steatosis.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div><i>C+ CT:&nbsp;&nbsp;25 HU less than the spleen in the <u><b>portal venous phase</b></u> suggests steatosis</i></div><br><div><i>(Avoid initially dx'ing hepatic steatotis on non-portal venous phases)</i></div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	c8b85863-6433-4bf3-b8e6-7c011a9547bf	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Evaluation of <b>hepatic steatosis</b> is {{c1::less::less or more}} reliable on C+ CT compared to noncontrast CT and requires an attenuation difference of <b>≥{{c2::25}} HU</b> less than the spleen<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Due to different contrast uptake rates of the liver and the spleen.</div>			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	afb9693f-d907-4356-bcd7-145208bc6386	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>MRI can determine if <b>hepatic steatosis</b> is present and can provide a rough gauge as to its severity.&nbsp;</div><br><div>{{c1::In- and out-of-phase::Sequences of}} GRE MRI imaging can more accurately quantify the degree of steatosis, although {{c2::liver biopsy::procedure}} is the gold standard and best evaluates for the presence of steatohepatitis and early fibrotic change.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	"<div><i>Can tell out of phase by looking for india ink / black border sign&nbsp;</i></div><br><div><img src=""4d77cdc50ef869914b5849278c698c0a.webp""><img src=""bc76a818bf93116844d5048b0523c6f3.webp""><br></div><div>In and out of phase&nbsp;</div><div>rID: 100039<br></div><br><div><i>""The India ink artifact, also known as the black boundary artifact, is&nbsp;a chemical shift artifact that can appear as a sharp black line or ink-like boundary on out-of-phase MRI images""</i><br></div><div><i>(Radiopaedia)</i></div>"			"<img src=""596c81c9047cbe5714d2f4deba3aafa1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	fbabbb4d-cfe3-4ab6-a9d3-eba2265dfb35	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0099 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>{{c1::Diffuse hepatic steatosis::diagnosis}}: In-<i> (left)</i> and out-of-phase<i> (right)</i> images demonstrate <u>diffuse signal loss</u> of the liver parenchyma on out-of-phase images.&nbsp;<br></div><br><div><img src=""060a5b3ee263a946631db1d77ee33953.webp""><img src=""fa724ef9ee93115616918ec0ef7705af.webp""><br></div><div><b></b></div>"	<div>When water-protons and fat-protons are present in the same&nbsp;MR voxel, the fat and water signals are summed in the in-phase images and subtracted in the out-of-phase&nbsp;images, leading to decrease in signal (hypointensity).<br></div>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	14a5e0c9-6207-4dde-912a-cebda357a0d1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>In in- and out-of-phase GRE MRI, signals from water-protons and fat-protons present in the same&nbsp;MR voxel are {{c1::summed}} in the in-phase images and {{c1::subtracted}} in the out-of-phase&nbsp;images.<br></div><br><div><img src=""060a5b3ee263a946631db1d77ee33953.webp""><img src=""fa724ef9ee93115616918ec0ef7705af.webp""><br></div><div><b></b></div>"	<div>Example shown: Hepatic steatosis leads to decreased signal on out-of-phase MRI due to subtraction of water and fat signal&nbsp;<br></div>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	718f06be-453b-4111-a54c-a10a4bfbf20e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Steatosis</u><br></div><br><div>Variations in {{c1::portal venous::vessel}} supply may cause <u>geographic regions</u> that are affected to a greater or lesser degree by fatty change.&nbsp;<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	0b831984-4873-42fc-873a-cbe0fafe393e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Steatosis</u><br></div><br><div><b>Focal fat</b> does <u>not</u> have any {{c1::mass effect::finding seen with masses}}, and {{c1::vessels::structures}} characteristically run through it undisturbed.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	008d8137-1999-4f79-a4b6-760db521f56f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><u>Hepatic Steatosis</u><br></div><br><div><b>Focal fat </b>tends to occur in the following typical locations and distributions:</div><div><br><ol><li>{{c1::Gallbladder fossa (drained by gallbladder vein)}}</li><li>{{c2::Subcapsular (along the falciform ligament)}}</li><li>{{c3::Periportal}}</li></ol><br><br><span style=""text-align: left;"">It may also be nodular and dispersed throughout the liver.</span><br></div>"	<br>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	490ccfb9-ecfc-4d5b-9cf5-739805cc5f8b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>MRI: Masslike region demonstrates <u>signal loss on out-of-phase image</u> <i>(right) </i>relative to in-phase image<i> (left)</i>;&nbsp; no mass effect and vessels run through region</div><br><div><img src=""b8361ee1864e06e3b7cdee24c33ce739.webp""><img src=""4fc1d15788715a37b8ca33243eddd724.webp""><br></div><br><div>Ultrasound: <u>Echogenic mass</u> in the medial left hepatic lobe (different patient and location)</div><br><div><img src=""94bf7e622be3d795f67e771e505c64d1.webp""><br></div><br><div>Diagnosis: {{c1::Focal fat (hepatic steatosis)}}</div><div><b></b></div>"	<br>			"<img src=""ab660b6210d6e890bff25400546db07d.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	ed011050-009a-4479-a461-763dbff61873	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0100 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>Regardless of the etiology, the iron-overloaded liver is {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>intense</u> on all MRI sequences relative to the&nbsp;{{c2::<u>paraspinal muscles</u>}}&nbsp;as an internal control.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div><u>signal dropout</u> on in-phase images</div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	bab36f74-199d-4223-a4dc-5ecb7eb1df5b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div><b>Signal dropout</b> is seen on&nbsp;{{c1::in::in- or out-of}}-phase images.</div><div><b></b></div>	<div><i>Opposite of steatosis</i><br></div><br><div><i>also hypointense on all MRI sequences</i></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	dd84b3fe-15ad-430f-b2e8-6c2ecff5bc38	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>The two pathways to <u>excess hepatic iron accumulation</u> are&nbsp;{{c1::primary hemochromatosis::genetic disease}} and&nbsp;{{c1::secondary hemochromatosis::acquired disease}}.</div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	164477ca-8d02-4ed8-8fd5-d2104c30d77e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>{{c1::Primary hemochromatosis::Disease}} is the most common cause of <u>iron overload</u>, due to a genetic defect causing increased iron absorption through the GI tract.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	5bc65ede-971e-459c-9172-4678ff6ecf0d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>In <b>{{c2::primary hemochromatosis::disease}}</b>, excess iron is deposited in <u>hepatocytes</u>, pancreas, myocardium, skin, and joints.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Excess iron in hepatocytes can cause {{c1::cirrhosis::liver pathology}}.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div><u>not</u> deposited in the Kupffer cells that make up the intrahepatic RES<br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	6ebb2c32-10fa-46bf-afe3-c65ce151feb6	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>In <b>{{c2::primary hemochromatosis}}</b>, <u>liver and pancreas</u> are <u>markedly T2 hypointense</u> and show <u>signal dropout</u> on in-phase images.</div><br><div>The <u>spleen and bone marrow</u> are <u>normal</u> since the {{c3:: (RES) reticuloendothelial}} system is not involved.&nbsp;</div><div><b></b></div>	<div><i>vs secondary hemochromatosis (hemosiderosis) where iron does accumulate in the liver RES</i><br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	f7057d28-309b-4de3-9147-08c7651a5e88	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>Treatment of <b>primary hemochromatosis</b> is {{c1::phlebotomy}}.</div><div><b></b></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	0184cce8-011a-490d-94ba-09e3acb9b7cf	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>Diagnosis: <b>{{c1::Primary hemochromatosis}}</b></div><br><div>Axial T2-weighted MRI demonstrates <u>diffuse low T2 signal</u> in the <u>liver and&nbsp;pancreas</u> with associated <i>signal loss</i> on in-phase <br>imaging <i>(not shown)</i>.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Spleen and bone marrow are normal.<br></div><br><div><img src=""967b481b99dcf3c9c7446ae77b3be2c1.webp""><br></div><div><b></b></div>"	<br>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	9f182484-ea3d-432c-85f7-02f800ab62db	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::Secondary hemochromatosis::Acquired disease}}</b>&nbsp;is usually seen in diseases that cause {{c2::hemosiderosis}}, where excess iron accumulates in the<b> (RES) reticuloendothelial system</b>.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>This may be due to&nbsp;<u>frequent blood transfusions or defective erythrocytosis</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	a43c9702-27cd-4275-aa47-8eb5d5cb1d81	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>Treatment of <b>hemosiderosis</b> /<b> secondary hemochromatosis</b> is with {{c1::iron chelators}}.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div><i>unlike primary hemochromatosis, which is treated with phlebotomy&nbsp;</i><br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	de32a5a2-715e-4d06-a9a0-67428f48dd69	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>The reticuloendothelial system (RES) has a large capacity for iron.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Therefore, iron stored in the RES is generally not harmful and the liver is normal in morphology <u>without</u> {{c1::cirrhosis::pathology}}.&nbsp;<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>However, when the RES becomes overwhelmed with iron, hepatocytes store iron as well <u>which can lead to cirrhosis</u><br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	190893b3-028c-42a3-b566-bcc097532fd1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Hepatic Iron Overload</u><br></div><br><div>In MRI of&nbsp;<b>hemosiderosis,</b>&nbsp;the {{c1::spleen::organ}} and {{c1::bone marrow::tissue}} will also appear <u>hypointense</u> due to increased iron stores throughout the entire <u>reticuloendothelial system</u>.&nbsp;</div><br><div>The {{c2::pancreas::organ}} is <i>spared</i>.<br></div><div><b></b></div>	<div>Also demonstrates a <u>hypointense liver</u> on conventional MRI sequences and <u>signal dropout</u> on in-phase images, as in hemochromatosis.<br></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	3b3f7c2e-12c0-4ce2-a73a-5dd73ad07a43	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Mnemonic to remember MRI of <b>Primary</b> v. <b>Secondary Hemochromatosis</b>:</div><br><div>Primary =&nbsp;{{c1::Pancreas::P}}</div><div>Secondary =&nbsp;{{c2::Spleen::S}}</div>	<div>Spleen spared in primary due to no RES involvement<br></div><br><div><i>Presumptive explanation of why spleen is spared in primary is that the RES (Kuppfer cells, spleen, bone marrow) is not primarily storing iron as in secondary&nbsp;</i></div>			"<img src=""5f5914c3af4c12a7f78fe9b274613c24.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	ea734961-2198-461b-89cb-1a4b3b7a45eb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0101 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>Abnormal extracellular deposition of <b>amyloid protein</b> in the liver can cause <i>focal</i> or <i>diffuse</i> areas of {{c1::<u>decreased</u>::increased / decreased}}<u> attenuation</u> on CT imaging.<br></div>	"<div><img src=""b0212078d150649e0169405be63a1c44.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""86bd222933c996f54f8e6987141fc8d1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Diffuse Parenchymal Liver Disease	ae6a3ce4-05b0-4a22-bfdf-70d444ee4d0a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0102 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::Cirrhosis::Disease}} is the replacement of functioning hepatocytes with dysfunctional fibrotic tissue, caused by repeated cycles of injury and repair.&nbsp;</div>	<div>Etiologies include <u>metabolic</u> (alcohol,</div><div>steatohepatitis, hemochromatosis, or Wilson disease), infectious (chronic hepatitis B or C),</div><div>or <u>inflammatory</u> (primary biliary cirrhosis or primary sclerosing cholangitis)</div>			"<img src=""30c2325444624e11de48044bf0d0db65.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Cirrhosis	6eeaf727-5471-4cce-9606-74456516c21d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0103 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The hallmarks of <b>cirrhosis</b> are <u>disorganized attempted regeneration</u> in the form of {{c1::nodules}} and {{c1::fibrosis}}.<br></div>	<div>Etiologies include <u>metabolic</u> (alcohol,</div><div>steatohepatitis, hemochromatosis, or Wilson disease), infectious (chronic hepatitis B or C),</div><div>or <u>inflammatory</u> (primary biliary cirrhosis or primary sclerosing cholangitis)</div>			"<img src=""30c2325444624e11de48044bf0d0db65.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Cirrhosis	f1a0a291-21e5-4dcc-b8ca-fdd5fa2b854d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0103 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>A caudate to right lobe size ratio (C/RL) of &gt;{{c1::0.65}} highly suggests <b>cirrhosis</b>.&nbsp;<br></div>	"<div>Caudate-right lobe ratio (C/RL) is taken at an axial slice&nbsp;<b>immediately below the bifurcation of the main portal vein</b>, 3 lines are drawn as below:<br></div><br><div><img src=""667b9c9ab38e1c413a36b73cb216609a.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""4a183a708c94dd0ed8d78a441f770a0a.webp""><br></div><br><div><ul><li><div><strong>line 1:&nbsp;</strong>parasagittal line drawn through the right lateral border of the main portal vein</div></li><li><div><strong>line 2:</strong>&nbsp;parasagittal line drawn through the left lateral border of the caudate lobe</div></li><li><div><strong>line 3:</strong>&nbsp;line orthogonal to lines 1 and 2 midway between the main portal vein and the inferior vena cava extended to the right liver edge</div></li><li><div><strong>caudate measurement (C):</strong>&nbsp;along line 3, between lines 1 and 2</div></li><li><div><strong>right lobe measurement (RL):</strong>&nbsp;along line 3, from right liver edge to line 1</div></li><li><div><strong>caudate-right lobe ratio:</strong>&nbsp;C/RL</div></li></ul><br><div>Interpretation</div><div><br><ul><li><div>C/RL &lt;0.6 = normal (does not exclude cirrhosis)&nbsp;</div></li><li><div>C/RL 0.6-0.65 = borderline</div></li><li><div>C/RL &gt;0.65 = 96% likely to be cirrhotic</div></li><li><div>C/RL &gt;0.73 = 99% likely to be cirrhotic</div></li></ul></div></div><br><div>As discussed previously, the caudate drains directly to the IVC, not via the hepatic veins, which is initially protective against cirrhosis.</div><br><div>Fundamentals of Body MRI</div>"			"<img src=""30c2325444624e11de48044bf0d0db65.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Cirrhosis	57663435-7a11-404c-9da0-935616ed87b8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0103 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::<b>MR elastography</b>}} is a non-invasive technique in which the patient wears a device resting over their right hepatic lobe which transmits {{c2::mechanical waves at a fixed frequency}}.</div><br><div>A phase-contrast pulse sequence with motion-encoding gradients is obtained which allows measurement of&nbsp;{{c3::stiffness}} in kPa<br></div>	"<div>Motion-encoding gradients measure micron-level tissue deformation in response to the stimulus.&nbsp;<br></div><br><div>Liver stiffness in kPa is measured by drawing ROI on the elastogram images.<br></div><br><div><img src=""58c6645606f89f55b908259b616379c8.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""ce3ccea4e3f2637b884e9e9eef8b69a2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Cirrhosis	64240592-1e5e-48eb-adde-8d4a1b9560c8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0104 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><b>HCC</b> is often <u>locally invasive</u> and tends to invade into the {{c1::<u>portal</u>}} and {{c1::<u>hepatic</u>}}<u> veins</u>, {{c1::<u>IVC</u>}}, and {{c1::<u>bile ducts</u>}}.</div><br><div>In contrast, cholangiocarcinoma and metastases to the liver are <i>much less likely</i> to do invade these structures.<br></div>	"<div><div>Arterially enhancing mass (HCC) invading the IVC and extending into the right atrium&nbsp;</div></div><br><div><img src=""dc2d8893a90a9ff512d50bf178062d0f.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""75aad025fadf2d527131e1005b830e97.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""a3d178446a3eacc25c4e9b90af030384.webp""></div><div>rID: 42243</div>"			"<img src=""8d433eff29106617315c388bfa5545e1.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	80121078-3cf4-468b-9f8d-a3462f88dab5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0106 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::LI-RADS}} is an imaging reporting and classification system for HCC on CT and MRI which is an indication of the relative risk of HCC.<br></div>	<div>The&nbsp;Liver&nbsp;Imaging Reporting and&nbsp;Data System (LI-RADS) is a classification system for liver lesions which is <b>used in patients with liver cirrhosis and chronic HBV without cirrhosis</b>, because these patients have an increased risk of&nbsp;hepatocellular&nbsp;carcinoma (HCC).</div><br><div>The LI-RADS&nbsp;category reflects the&nbsp;probability&nbsp;of HCC and is based on the typical CT and MR-findings in HCC.<br></div><br><div><div><b>LI-RADS is not meant to be used in patients &lt;18 years or patients with cirrhosis due to congenital hepatic fibrosis or due to vascular disorders</b>, because these patients have a lower chance of developing HCC.</div></div><br><div>Radiology Assistant</div>			"<img src=""cbc54f9340ce301ea8898ebf3db81607.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	00a584ac-20d9-4682-b9fe-46d21f5e7f46	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0107 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>LI-RADS</b> is only used in people with {{c1::risk factors for HCC (chronic hepatitis infections, cirrhosis)}} but excluding those with&nbsp;{{c2::cirrhosis due to cardiac or vascular etiologies}}.</div>	<br>			"<img src=""cbc54f9340ce301ea8898ebf3db81607.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	3da7f1e0-0b72-43b8-95ad-8858ac30e2ef	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0107 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div><b><u>LI-RADS Major criteria for HCC</u>:</b></div><br><ol><li>{{c1::Arterial phase hyperenhancement}}</li><li>{{c2::Non-peripheral washout on portal venous and delayed phases}}</li><li>{{c3::Enhancing capsule/pseudocapsule seen in portal venous or delayed phases}}</li><li>{{c4::Threshold growth with diameter increase of &gt;50% in &lt;6 months}}</li><li>{{c8::Size}} (different cutoffs depending on enhancement pattern)</li></ol></div><br><div><b><u>Ancillary Findings Favoring HCC</u>:</b></div><div><br><div><div style=""""><ol><li>{{c5::Non-enhancing}} capsule</li><li>{{c6::Nodule-in-nodule}} architecture</li><li>{{c6::Mosaic}} architecture</li><li>{{c7::Fat}} in mass</li><li>{{c7::Blood products}} in mass</li></ol></div></div></div>"	"<img src=""7a1441cc39aad329e3074615b128a4e4.webp""><img src=""d9a7cc21a4b89b0b19342b0747d9bbeb.webp""><br><br>LI-RADS major features: <br>There are five major features which are typically seen in HCC in patients with liver cirrhosis and  chronic hepatitis B virus infection<br><br><span>The 2018 version of LI-RADS describe</span><span>s major and ancillary criteria: the major imaging criteria lead to the assignment of the LI-RADS score, while the ancillary findings may be used as tie breakers.<br></span><br><i>Radiology Assistant</i>"			"<img src=""cbc54f9340ce301ea8898ebf3db81607.webp"">"					"Major criteria for HCC:<br><img src=""2834eaf291ac48d58741a54087a5c5ea.webp""><br><br>Ancillary findings favoring HCC:<br><img src=""0cf39b168730af5ba71a278594668b77.webp""><br><br><i>Radiology Assistant</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	fef4c855-93a6-44e7-81d6-a1fac2082100	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0107 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><div><div><b>{{c1::Fibrolamellar}} carcinoma</b> is a rare subtype of <b>HCC</b> that occurs in young patients <u>without cirrhosis</u>.</div><br><div>The tumor tends to be <u>large</u> when diagnosed but has a <i>better prognosis</i> than typical HCC.&nbsp;<br></div></div></div>	"<img src=""5a0e29e44112763ddd20d43e4204ff09.webp"">"			"<img src=""cbc54f9340ce301ea8898ebf3db81607.webp"">"					"<img src=""fa37fa40d6a82c56d163bbcc3ed45a9c.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	557ee207-f450-416f-bafc-87712a476238	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0107 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><div><div>On imaging, <b>fibrolamellar HCC</b> is a large, heterogeneous liver mass.</div><br><div>A {{c1::fibrotic central scar::characteristic finding}} is classic, which is <u>hypointense</u> on T1- and T2-weighted MRI images.</div><br><div>{{c2::Capsular retraction::Morphologic finding}} may be seen in 10%.<br></div></div></div>	"<div><span>in contrast, FNH</span><span>&nbsp;features a T2 <u>hyperintense</u> scar that <u>enhances late</u></span></div><br><div><img src=""5a0e29e44112763ddd20d43e4204ff09.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""cbc54f9340ce301ea8898ebf3db81607.webp"">"					"<img src=""fa37fa40d6a82c56d163bbcc3ed45a9c.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	d191897c-9906-4fe3-b093-ff882ad176a0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0107 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
