<div><div><div><b>{{c1::Mass-forming::type of}} cholangiocarcinoma</b>&nbsp;is one of three recognized macroscopic growth patterns of <u>intrahepatic</u> cholangiocarcinomas and usually presents as</div><br><div><ol><li>&nbsp;{{c2::<u>Large</u>::small/large}} and relatively {{c2::well::well/poorly}}-defined hepatic mass with <u>lobulated</u> margins</li><li>{{c3::<u>Delayed/progressive</u>}} enhancement*</li><li>Peripheral biliary dilatation</li></ol></div></div></div>	"<div>*Enhancement pattern is variable, may see hepatobiliary phase washout rather than delayed enhancement</div><br><div><img src=""1a8b0a70f36f45ae555d6e9072846cbb.webp""></div><br><div>Three subtypes of macroscopic growth (Radiopaedia):</div><br><ol><li><b>mass-forming</b>: definite mass in the liver parenchyma</li><li><b>periductal-infiltrating</b>: extends longitudinally along the bile duct, often causing peripheral bile duct dilation</li><li><b>intraductal</b>: proliferates in the lumen of the bile duct-like a papilla or&nbsp;tumor thrombus</li></ol><br><div>Are also characterized by peripheral high DWI due to hypercellularity</div>"			"<img src=""281eaad1c88467e749098f2bea89146f.webp"">"					"<img src=""004e7e764a75c212f0df508841d90169.webp""><img src=""76b32ab602a2e2f9a72fb3cc56f8b0a4.webp""><img src=""8c02a22b275b0ddfc6f4f681fda116ee.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	c6e12e01-d3fc-4e71-ac31-5c99cc068b3a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0108 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

"<div><img src=""9889d1825261e527c5e28b1805770bb3.webp""><img src=""112e0f443fa3fbd76a7e9a41fc5225e1.webp""><br></div><br><div>{{c1::<b>Hepatic lymphoma</b>}}: PET/CT demonstrates a single defined <u>low density hepatic lesion</u> <i>(→, left)</i> and more diffuse low density changes of the liver parenchyma with <u>remarkable FDG avidity</u> <i>(right)</i><br></div><br><div>MRI shows <u>restricted diffusion</u></div><br><div>Associated splenomegaly and lymphadenopathy</div>"	<br>			"<img src=""d69dc68d2bcb5a3f32eed1a68e0e4fce.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	28eb6920-1120-43ac-a83b-12a74f46ee2a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0108 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Primary hepatic lymphoma</b> is {{c1::<u>very rare</u>::rare/common}} and may present as a single mass or multiple masses.</div><br><div>They tend to be infiltrative and {{c2::<u>preserve</u>::preserve/disrupt}}<u> hepatic vasculature</u>.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""d69dc68d2bcb5a3f32eed1a68e0e4fce.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	e2f81b59-cb31-4e9a-a28f-aeca65ee24e2	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0108 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Lymphomatous involvement of the liver</b> tends to be secondary to systemic disease, with associated {{c1::splenomegaly::organ finding}} and {{c1::lymphadenopathy::associated finding}}.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""d69dc68d2bcb5a3f32eed1a68e0e4fce.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	3fb5fe9c-1ecd-498d-8666-a9097b76b882	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0108 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On CT and MRI, <b>hepatic lymphoma</b> is {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>enhancing</u>/dense and tends to show {{c2::<u>restricted diffusion</u>}} on MRI.</div>	"<img src=""828ec4a5a3bb68175e712d8aee32f0b3.webp""><br><br><i>non-Hodgkin lymphoma with hepatic involvement (</i>rID: 15868)"			"<img src=""d69dc68d2bcb5a3f32eed1a68e0e4fce.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	8a85b911-92cc-4089-9831-c0051f476c34	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0109 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On ultrasound, <b>hepatic lymphoma </b>tends to be {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>echoic</u> and may have the <i>{{c1::target}} sign</i> typical of metastases.<br></div>	"<img src=""1fa74b077c95af9c15f0a8f4daa4659a.webp""><br><br>Example of a hepatic lymphoma, no target sign on this image<br><br>rID: 94408"			"<img src=""d69dc68d2bcb5a3f32eed1a68e0e4fce.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	2c07ba33-c7f1-4de6-91e5-d5061dbafaa4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0109 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>{{c1::Post transplant lymphoproliferative disorder (PTLD)::Hepatic malignancy}} appears as a mass with a variable and nonspecific appearance.</div><br><div>Therefore, it is important to consider {{c1::PTLD}} in the differential&nbsp;if a liver mass is seen in a <u>transplant patient</u>.&nbsp;<br></div><div><img src=""c6994c092a1442849efbe72fce4d3716.webp""><br></div>"	"<i>PTLD can occur in the:<br><ol><li>Abdomen (liver, small bowel, colon, stomach)</li><li>Chest (lung)</li><li>Head and neck</li><li>CNS</li><li>Cutaneous</li><li>Osseous (rare)</li></ol><div>(Radiopaedia)</div><br><div><b>Imaging Findings:&nbsp;</b>18 year old man post liver transplant.</div></i><i><div><div><div>CT shows multiple small round masses representing Post Transplant Proliferative disorder (PTLD). "<div><img src=""4b5637eab6181be614dbd572849b2a06.webp""><br></div><br><div>{{c1::Epithelioid hemangioendothelioma}}: Multisequence MRI shows multiple <u>T1 hypointense</u>, <u>T2 hyperintense</u>&nbsp;hepatic lesions with <u>peripheral target pattern enhancement</u> <i>(<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;→</span>)</i>, predominant <u>peripheral distribution</u>, and associated <u>capsular retraction</u> <i>(not shown)</i>.<br></div>"	<div>rare vascular malignancy that characteristically</div><div>causes multiple spherical subcapsular masses than can become confluent</div><br><div>The individual masses may have a <u>halo</u> or <u>target appearance</u></div>			"<img src=""18a8fbf0c5772c9de19b7395341dcdad.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	12a9ba91-1257-4f2c-ae5d-d6eb97920dc9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0110 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>{{c1::Epithelioid hemangioendothelioma}} is a rare vascular malignancy that characteristically causes <u>multiple T1 hypointense</u>, <u>T2 hyperintense</u> <u>spherical subcapsular masses</u> that can become confluent.</div><br><div>The individual masses may have a <u>halo</u> or <u>target appearance</u>.</div></div>	"<div><img src=""4b5637eab6181be614dbd572849b2a06.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""18a8fbf0c5772c9de19b7395341dcdad.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	434f51b5-549a-462c-987b-2f6b9a9258a0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0110 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Epithelioid hemangioendothelioma </b>has a predominantly&nbsp;{{c1::peripheral::central/peripheral}} distribution in the liver.</div></div>	"<div><img src=""4b5637eab6181be614dbd572849b2a06.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""18a8fbf0c5772c9de19b7395341dcdad.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	fbde2bcc-e7b8-438d-8a7d-a714d89068ae	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0110 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The differential of liver&nbsp;<u>capsular retraction</u> includes:</div><div><br><ul><li>{{c1::Mass-forming cholangiocarcinoma::Malignancy}}</li><li>{{c2::Fibrolamellar HCC (seen in 10% of cases of fibrolamellar HCC)::Malignancy}}</li><li>{{c3::Epithelioid hemangioendothelioma::Malignancy}}</li><li>{{c4::Pseudocirrhosis}} (macronodular liver contour with capsular retraction due to treated metastases)</li><li>{{c5::Confluent hepatic fibrosis}} (wedge-shaped fibrosis that may be seen in cirrhosis)</li></ul></div>	<br>			"<img src=""18a8fbf0c5772c9de19b7395341dcdad.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Malignant Hepatic Masses	31de33d3-4904-4d55-b6ca-649a4f28055b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0110 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><img src=""84607ae7b75678c05ef082662b57fbd2.webp""><img src=""b251b18bcd230aa82b5b4caf4fdcd379.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""82cf620d842eebdaf762b9c17453787f.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""9cb340fc60a0a9c98bf74aa81f85a507.webp""></div><br><div>Dynamic T1 C+ MRI (early arterial to delayed phase) shows  {{c2::<u>peripheral discontinuous nodular</u>}} <u>enhancement</u> with progressively increasing {{c3::<u>centripetal</u>}}&nbsp;<u>enhancement</u> on delayed images. The signal intensity of the peripheral enhancement is similar to that of the aorta.</div><div><br>Hyperintense on T2-weighted image (fourth image)<br></div><br><div>Diagnosis:&nbsp;{{c1::Hemangioma}}</div>"				"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	8e4ba6ab-641d-416e-aa37-492bbfcda204	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Hepatic cavernous hemangioma}} is the most common benign hepatic neoplasm.</div><br><div>It is composed of <u>disorganized endothelial cell-lined pockets of blood vessels</u>, supplied by a peripheral branch of the hepatic artery.</div>				"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	d4a96650-9c45-47b4-a4b3-81838c067985	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hemangioma</b> is more common in {{c1::females::sex}} and {{c2::uncommon::common/uncommon}} in cirrhosis.&nbsp;<br></div>	<div>When a known hemangioma is sequentially followed in a patient with early cirrhosis, the hemangioma <b>involutes as the liver becomes more cirrhotic</b><br></div>			"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	1da7dd6b-7aca-45a2-8ede-3fee00e5ea9c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hemangioma</b> may range in size from &lt;1 cm to &gt;10 cm.</div><br><div>Giant hemangiomas tend to have a {{c2::non-enhancing central area::characteristic appearance}} representing {{c1::cystic degeneration / myxoid tissue}}.<br></div>	"<div><img src=""98de0bb4d2f77c582e0a6095d25b5cb2.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""5108aae0f7dcc35161a4533edb3d44a3.webp""><br></div><div><i>1: Arterial phase showing cystic components prior to enhancement</i></div><div><div><i>2: Portal venous phase showing typical pooling peripheral enhancement</i></div><br><div><i>Radiopaedia</i></div></div>"			"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	972fa043-9d38-46b6-87fe-99c888228c0b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On CT and MRI, a virtually pathognomonic imaging feature for <b>hemangioma&nbsp;</b>is {{c1::peripheral discontinuous progressive nodular::pattern}}&nbsp;enhancement.</div><br><div>The degree of enhancement should <u>match the blood pool</u> on all images and demonstrate gradual {{c2::centripetal::direction}} fill-in on later phases.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	063161f1-339e-4d5b-bc81-e3988a06923f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The <u>noncontrast</u> CT appearance of <b>hemangioma</b> is {{c1::not helpful::helpful / not helpful}}.<br></div>	<div>A hemangioma appears as a nonspecific hypoattenuating liver mass.<br></div>			"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	4cebecc7-42c9-4a6c-a52f-f051d079bb24	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On MRI, hemangiomas are typically T2 {{c1::hyper}}intense and become even more {{c1::hyper}}intense on T2-fat saturated images compared to conventional T2-weighted images.<br></div>	"<div><img src=""0978eafeee19aa593b6f8d01049a0510.webp""><br></div><div>Case courtesy of Frank Gaillard, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 8155<br></div>"			"<img src=""92811bf693ab366f1ed725d9cf8ac916.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	3e3e30a4-5146-426f-a8a3-560ac8f94ae5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The classic ultrasound appearance of a <b>hepatic hemangioma</b> is a {{c1::circumscribed::circumscribed or poorly circumscribed}}, {{c1::homo::homo/hetero}}geneously <u>echogenic</u> mass with {{c2::no flow::flow/no flow}} on color Doppler.</div><br><div>Posterior {{c3::acoustic enhancement}} may be present.&nbsp;<br></div>	"<div><img src=""0f7792876f35a9cd4c9308f080442739.webp"">&nbsp;<img src=""194600d29af7bd6fc1de54e86c227bd8.webp""></div><div>Case courtesy of Frank Gaillard, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 10878<br></div>"			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	045a6185-2b39-4afb-95d3-b55b178af02f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0111 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>If a <u>solitary</u>,&nbsp;<u>classic-appearing</u> {{c1::hemangioma::circumscribed, homogenously echogenic mass with no flow on color Doppler}} is seen on ultrasound and the patient has an otherwise&nbsp;normal-appearing liver, normal LFTs, no known malignancy or risk factors for HCC, and is&nbsp;asymptomatic, then <u>no further workup is required</u>.<br></div>	"<div><i>Exception: echogenic fatty livers (may appear hypoechoic relative to parenchyma)</i></div><div><img src=""f0bcc4e144d04c9655cc447645ed020c.webp""><br></div>"			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	a007c669-ca4e-41ce-bc5b-ad16275fd04e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>A {{c1::hypoechoic halo::finding}} <i>(target sign)</i> on ultrasound should <u>never</u> be seen in a <b>hemangioma</b> – this finding suggests <u>malignancy</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	8cba3bf6-41c0-49ca-831f-47587aefcb89	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Ultrasound&nbsp;appearance of <b>hemangioma</b> can be confusing in a patient with <u>underlying fatty liver</u> and may appear&nbsp;relatively&nbsp;<i>{{c1::hypo}}echoic</i> compared to the background of&nbsp;<i>{{c1::hyper}}echoic</i> fatty liver.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	0465d813-4db6-4a4e-bdee-a2a807a28bcd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Any <u>heterogeneity</u> or <u>atypical ultrasound findings</u> should prompt consideration of an alternative diagnosis <u>other than</u><b> hemangioma&nbsp;</b>such as {{c1::hyperechoic HCC}} or {{c1::metastatic disease}}&nbsp;<i>(even in the absence of a halo)</i>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<div>Suspicion should be high as HCC does not have a characteristic US appearance. Especially if it is &gt; 1 cm or enlarging.</div><div><br><div>In a patient with cirrhosis or any known primary malignancy, further workup (MRI or CT) is usually warranted.</div></div><div><br><div>** Hemangioma tends to regress in size in cirrhotic livers</div></div>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	bcf5b95e-215c-494b-a983-94efbf0daa55	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><b>{{c2::Focal nodular hyperplasia (FNH)}} </b>is a {{c1::hamartoma::type of tumor}} consisting of disorganized liver tissue with <u>no malignant potential</u>.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"					"<img src=""b39faf773c43dc64be8bcbf1a189750b.webp""><img src=""49de171fa755227d378e0186e326aabd.webp""><img src=""4e1d47e2b8a765ae568a57b86b07c325.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	8b937ae8-a5b6-43d5-96f8-b3eb0575dad1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>FNH</b> is more common in {{c1::women::sex}} and {{c2::is <u>not</u>::is/is not}} associated with oral contraceptives.<br></div>	<div><i>unlike hepatic adenomas which are probably associated with long-term OCP use</i><br></div>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"					"<img src=""b39faf773c43dc64be8bcbf1a189750b.webp""><img src=""49de171fa755227d378e0186e326aabd.webp""><img src=""4e1d47e2b8a765ae568a57b86b07c325.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	cd35d9a1-a68b-4790-851e-1055ad61f9d0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>FNH</b> is called a <i>stealth lesion</i> because it resembles {{c1::background liver parenchyma}} on all modalities, except {{c2::<u>arterial</u>}}<u> phase</u> imaging due to <u>vascular supply</u>.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	3a1009e4-7729-49c0-8d0d-697c5605766e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Approximately 15% of <b>FNH</b> have a characteristic {{c1::central scar}} consisting of {{c2::biliary ductules}} and {{c2::venules}}.<br></div>	Does not contain fibrotic tissue and therefore is not a true scar <br><br>vs fibrolamellar HCC which has a true fibrotic central scar that is hypointense on T1/T2<br><br>FNH scar is T2 hyperintense and enhances late			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"					"<img src=""b39faf773c43dc64be8bcbf1a189750b.webp""><img src=""49de171fa755227d378e0186e326aabd.webp""><img src=""4e1d47e2b8a765ae568a57b86b07c325.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	90df3f60-b8da-43af-bc4e-99b6e53dece7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>FNH</b> {{c1::does <u>not</u>::does / does not}} have a capsule.<br></div>				"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"					"<img src=""b39faf773c43dc64be8bcbf1a189750b.webp""><img src=""49de171fa755227d378e0186e326aabd.webp""><img src=""4e1d47e2b8a765ae568a57b86b07c325.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	938e886f-5bf7-4608-be45-5c1dce671d81	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>MRI with {{c1::Eovist contrast}} is the most useful imaging modality to diagnose <b>FNH</b>.<br></div>	"<span>Due to the presence of hepatocytes and&nbsp;</span><span><b>malformed biliary ductules that retain eovist</b><br><div><img src=""4e1d47e2b8a765ae568a57b86b07c325.webp""></div></span>"			"<img src=""a3399d07de05ecd6c88bdcc30f8a8791.webp"">"					"<img src=""b39faf773c43dc64be8bcbf1a189750b.webp""><img src=""49de171fa755227d378e0186e326aabd.webp""><br><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	f487951e-ea1f-4fc7-847d-b5d920275284	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0112 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>FNH</b> typically is {{c1::<u>iso</u>}}<u>intense</u> to liver on all MRI sequences, except it is <u>arterially hyperenhancing</u> and will show <u>retained Eovist enhancement</u> <u>iso- or hyper-intense</u> relative to liver in the {{c2::hepatobiliary}} phase (20 minutes after contrast administration).&nbsp;<br></div>	"<div>Due to the presence of hepatocytes and&nbsp;<b>malformed biliary ductules that retain Eovist</b><br></div><br><div><img src=""aaac9bf8161067afa003d016b9fc14ec.webp"" style=""width: 649.031px;""></div><div>FNH in a 30-year-old woman, with a typical appearance at MRI.&nbsp;(A)&nbsp;Axial MR image shows characteristic homogeneous arterial phase enhancement (APHE) (→) with a hypointense central scar (&gt;).&nbsp;(B)&nbsp;Axial MR image acquired with hepatocyte-specific contrast agent (HSCA) during the transitional phase shows near isointense enhancement (→), with a persistent hypointense central scar (&gt;), as opposed to the delayed hyperenhancement seen with extracellular contrast agents.&nbsp;(C)&nbsp;Axial MR image acquired 20 minutes after administration of HSCA during the hepatobiliary phase (HBP) shows characteristic homogeneous hyperintense uptake of contrast material (→), with a persistent hypointense central scar (&gt;).<br></div><br><div><img src=""16071e21ab1d805df4d73652894ba7c2.webp"" style=""width: 653.531px;""></div><div><i>Variable enhancement patterns:</i>&nbsp;(A)&nbsp;Coronal gadoxetate-enhanced MR image in a 47-year-old woman with FNH shows heterogeneous hyperintense uptake (→).&nbsp;(B)&nbsp;Axial gadoxetate-enhanced MR image in a 27-year-old woman shows homogeneous isointense uptake (→) in the FNH lesion, which is best identified by the hypointense central scar (&gt;).&nbsp;(C)&nbsp;Axial gadoxetate-enhanced MR image in a 65-year-old man shows a hypointense FNH, with peripheral ring uptake (→).<br></div><br><div>RadioGraphics</div>"			"<img "<div>Doppler findings of <b>FNH</b> include a {{c1::spoke-wheel}} configuration of arterial vessels.<br></div><br><div><img src=""2d002ca1dc8876b8159a722599ed197d.webp""><br></div>"	<div>Case courtesy of Bouhouche Abdeldjalil, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 167496<br></div>			"<img src=""e3ccbacab71ca1a2607c375ab5426fcc.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	8c2ebb31-cee0-4cce-bb19-6e4b4fbc027f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0113 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Ultrasound findings of <b>FNH</b> are {{c1::nonspecific::specific/nonspecific}}.&nbsp;<br></div>	<div><span>The central scar is rarely seen on ultrasound, and even&nbsp;</span><span>when it is, this finding can be seen in other lesions, including <b>HCC, giant hemangioma, or&nbsp;</b></span><b><span>adenoma</span></b><br></div>			"<img src=""e3ccbacab71ca1a2607c375ab5426fcc.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	552be887-ea97-4a50-9daf-95452a5d56e4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0113 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Kupffer cells in <b>FNH</b> may be confirmed by a {{c1::sulfur colloid}} study (1/3 of the time) and bile duct cells can be visualized on a {{c2::HIDA}} scan.<br></div>	<span><div><u>Kupffer cells</u>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<u>bile ductules</u>&nbsp;are both present so nuclear medicine studies can be utilized to confirm the diagnosis.&nbsp;</div></span>			"<img src=""e3ccbacab71ca1a2607c375ab5426fcc.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	2eed00a1-1c42-4a16-8de6-8ab2621bdf12	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0113 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><img src=""a7cb87c3f032712b868f8fc70a9bfb92.webp"" style=""text-align: start;""><br></div><br><div>{{c1::Hepatic adenoma::diagnosis}}<br></div>"				"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	1e47ac97-46da-4327-ba6b-2814a5ce819d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hepatic adenoma </b>is a benign hepatic neoplasm containing {{c1::hepatocytes::cell type}} and scattered {{c2::Kupffer cells::cell type}}, and no bile ducts.</div>				"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	3ab7f3a8-b89c-4f91-8afa-8e6ac84aac54	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>HIDA scan of <b>focal nodular hyperplasia</b>:&nbsp;{{c1::Positive::+/-}}</div><br><div>HIDA scan of <b>hepatic adenoma</b>:&nbsp;{{c1::Negative::+/-}}<br></div>	The absence of bile ducts makes a HIDA scan a useful test to distinguish between focal nodular hyperplasia (which contains bile ducts and would be positive on HIDA) verses a hepatic adenoma, which does not contain bile ducts and will show a paucity of uptake on HIDA.			"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	791ec337-7e84-4a5f-8dbe-9b114834a17f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hepatic adenomas </b>are much more common in {{c1::females::sex}}, especially with prolonged {{c2::oral contraceptive::medication class}} use.&nbsp;</div>	<br>			"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	9297129c-7846-4aef-8c33-0b2e5227fb0f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>When seen in males, <b>hepatic adenoma</b> may be associated with {{c1::anabolic steroid::medication class}} use.</div><br><div>Other associations include {{c2::collagen vascular}} disease and {{c3::type I glycogen storage}} disease&nbsp;</div>	<div>&nbsp;type 1 GSD = von Gierke disease</div>			"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	d68fd1d3-502b-4e1e-a60c-bc8982cba94c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>There are<b> </b><u>four histologic subtypes</u> of<b> hepatic adenomas&nbsp;</b>with varied imaging findings:</div><div><br><ol><li>{{c1::<b>Inflammatory</b>}}: Most common, has the highest {{c2::bleeding}} risk.</li><li>{{c3::<b>HNF-alpha 1 mutated</b>}}: Second most common, characterized by {{c4::multiple adenomas}}, associated with <u>FAP</u>&nbsp;and <u>von Gierke</u>.</li><li>{{c5::<b>Beta-catenin mutated</b>}}: Least common, seen in men on anabolic steroids, has the highest risk of malignant transformation.</li><li>{{c6::Unclassified}}</li></ol></div>	"<div><img src=""fdcee5161c7160c9320bd6beadbd3208.webp""><br></div><br><div><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i></div>"			"<img src=""6be5b824e2aea000ef4e44418c0b4ace.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	fca58a1b-10e9-4451-9b67-b856f27a86c6	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0114 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hepatic adenomas</b> have a relatively high risk of {{c1::<u>hemorrhage</u>::complication}}, which is often the presenting symptom.</div><br><div>For this reason, incidentally discovered adenomas &gt;{{c2::5}} cm are usually <u>resected</u>.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""9c66a39e886965d61b01e0b9546c05a3.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	34b0952d-e27b-424c-b4c4-c88b6f37fd43	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0115 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hepatic adenomas</b> are supplied by the {{c1::hepatic}} artery and thus tend to be<b> </b><u>hypervascular</u> on arterial phase.&nbsp;<br></div><br><div>Some subtypes (inflammatory) may demonstrate {{c2::<b>intralesional fat</b>}} which on MRI will demonstrate <u>T1 hyperintensity</u> and <u>signal loss</u> on out-of-phase images.&nbsp;</div>	"<div>Adenomas may&nbsp;be difficult to differentiate from other hypervascular liver lesions in the absence of fat or&nbsp;hemorrhage.<br></div><br><div><img src=""fdcee5161c7160c9320bd6beadbd3208.webp""><br></div><div><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i></div>"			"<img src=""9c66a39e886965d61b01e0b9546c05a3.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	aefe90c3-275d-42e3-b74e-a8cbf9081462	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0115 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Hepatic adenomas </b>are typically {{c1::well::well/poorly}} circumscribed masses with <u>arterial hyperenhancement</u>, becoming {{c2::<u>iso</u>}}- or {{c2::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>intense</u> to liver on portal venous and delayed phase imaging.&nbsp;<br></div><br><div>They may appear heterogeneous due to {{c3::fat::tissue}} or {{c3::hemorrhagic::tissue}} content. A {{c4::fibrous pseudocapsule}} may be present, which tends to <u>enhance late</u><br></div>	"<div>Each subtype has slightly different imaging features, making confident imaging diagnosis somewhat difficult and often requiring tissue sampling for confirmation.<br></div><br><div><i>In general&nbsp;<b>fibrous structures tend to enhance late</b></i><br></div><br><div><img src=""fdcee5161c7160c9320bd6beadbd3208.webp""><br></div><div><i>Fundamentals of Body MRI</i></div>"			"<img src=""9c66a39e886965d61b01e0b9546c05a3.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	2caf1584-1575-47d2-bf90-47cc860e0f92	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0115 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Is ultrasound useful for distinguishing <b>hepatic adenomas</b>?<br></div><br><div>{{c1::No::Yes/No}}<br></div>	<div>There are <u>no specific ultrasound features</u> to distinguish an adenoma from other hepatic masses</div><br><div>An adenoma may be hyperechoic, isoechoic, or hypoechoic relative to normal liver<br></div>			"<img src=""9c66a39e886965d61b01e0b9546c05a3.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	8782d225-d62b-41de-b1ef-f268a5ee4a54	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0115 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Is nuclear medicine useful for distinguishing <b>hepatic adenomas</b>?<br></div><br><div>{{c1::No::Yes/No}}<br></div>	<div>Adenomas are usually photopenic on Tc-99m sulfur colloid scintigraphy (in contrast to FNH), but not always.&nbsp;</div><br><div>There is usually <u>lack of uptake on a HIDA scan</u> due to the absence of biliary ductules<br></div>			"<img src=""9c66a39e886965d61b01e0b9546c05a3.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Benign Liver Masses	920db8c3-56d0-4a6b-8335-8d6b59d34ad3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0115 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>Does acute hepatitis usually present with normal or abnormal imaging findings?&nbsp;</div><br><div>{{c1::Normal}}<br></div>	<div>The most common imaging finding in acute hepatitis is of a normal liver.</div><br><div>When imaging is abnormal, the&nbsp;most common findings are periportal edema (starry sky pattern of increased portal triad&nbsp;echogenicity on ultrasound;&nbsp;</div><br><div>fluid on both sides of the portal vein on CT and MRI) and gallbladder wall thickening/edema<br></div>			"<img src=""dede2d804d690a57b6a16947ba0f1065.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	631c16e1-148e-4770-abc0-478613ec38b4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0116 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><b>Hepatic abscess</b> is most commonly caused by a {{c1::bowel::organ}} process and resultant infectious nidus carried through the {{c2::portal}} system to the liver.&nbsp;<br></div>	"<div>Common causes include diverticulitis,&nbsp;appendicitis, Crohn's disease, and bowel surgery. <div>Common causes of <b>hepatic abscess</b> include:</div><br><div><ol><li>{{c1::Diverticulitis}}</li><li>{{c3::Appendicitis}}</li><li>{{c4::Crohn's}} disease&nbsp;</li><li>{{c2::Bowel}} surgery</li></ol></div><br><div><i>E. coli</i> is the most common causative&nbsp;organism.</div>	"<div><div><img src=""0e0d99f651210a614dff8ff4e82c1340.webp""><br></div><div><div><div><div>CT demonstrates a large irregular fluid-density lesion within the right lobe of the liver with rim enhancement (<b>inner rim</b>) and a thin outer ring of hypoattenuation (""<b>double target</b>&nbsp;<b>sign</b>"").</div><br><div>There are multiple smaller peripheral lesions with similar characteristics. <div>Imaging features of <b>hepatic abscess </b>may mimic {{c1::<b>metastasis</b>}}, appearing as a <u>ring-enhancing mass</u> on CT and MRI.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Reactive perilesional <u>hyperenhancement</u> may be present. <div>On ultrasound, a <b>pyogenic liver abscess</b> starts as an ill-defined area of altered echogenicity ({{c2::phlegmon}} stage) which evolves into a well-defined {{c1::hypo}}echoic structure with {{c1::internal echoes}} ({{c2::mature abscess}}).</div>	"<div>Abscess with CT and MR correlates</div><br><div><img src=""6098783e0516c5d7a8073fb7ed69cede.webp""></div><br><div>Case courtesy of Bruno Di Muzio, Radiopaedia.org, rID: 62849</div>"			"<img src=""8d9b753ff56267bf06ee3fbe06938970.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	2235e8bc-08e1-46c0-9d13-b73fe1a8115b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0117 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Cholangitic abscess</b> can be seen with {{c1::<u>bacterial cholangitis</u>::infection}}, or may occur in patients with biliary stents, prior sphincterotomies or hepaticojejunostomies due to {{c2::gastrointestinal reflux into the biliary tree::mechanism}}.</div></div>				"<img src=""8d9b753ff56267bf06ee3fbe06938970.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	221c6550-1805-4d02-b05a-8bc0cce32b88	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0117 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><div><b>Liver TB</b> lesions may be micro- or macronodular <i>(rare)</i>, with multiple small {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>echoic</u> {{c1::<u>hypo</u>}}<u>enhancing</u> nodules or larger mass-like areas which demonstrate variable enhancement.</div><br><div>These findings are often accompanied by {{c2::hepatosplenomegaly::organ changes}}.<br></div></div>	"<img src=""ef40b64068ed4385cd7a25f1ac42fec7.webp""><br><br>Scattered small rounded well-defined hypodensities seen in the liver, spleen and both kidneys in a patient with disseminated TB, suggesting TB granulomas.&nbsp;<br>rID: 39290"			"<img src=""8d9b753ff56267bf06ee3fbe06938970.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	d647aee4-63a3-46f7-92a7-1b8ea93c639e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0117 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Hepatic fungal infections</b> typically show punctate, hypoenhancing {{c1::microabscesses}} on CT and MRI and tiny hypoechoic lesions on ultrasound.&nbsp;</div><br><div>Lesions are T2 {{c2::hyper}}intense and {{c2::<u>do</u>::do/do not}} restrict diffusion on MRI.</div><br><div>Prior asymptomatic exposure and/or treated disease may show punctate, echogenic {{c3::calcifications/granulomas}}.<br></div></div>	"<img src=""3342103bc9fa8c65e5175b7e4d167cc5.webp""><br>(Case of hepatic candidiasis rID: 9506)"			"<img src=""8d9b753ff56267bf06ee3fbe06938970.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	d2dc0515-138f-406f-8e8c-d5a666791a1b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0117 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Histoplasmosis</b> is another form of <b>{{c1::granulomatous}} hepatitis</b> secondary to the endemic fungus Histoplasma capsulatum which is most commonly found in the {{c2::Ohio}} and {{c2::Mississippi}} River Valleys.</div><br><div>It is more common in immunocompromised patients but can be seen in immunocompetent patients as well.<br></div></div>	<i>Granulomatous hepatitis similar to TB infection</i>			"<img src=""8d9b753ff56267bf06ee3fbe06938970.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Hepatic Infection	435680cd-e5e6-4206-a650-74fe08f3bc7a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0117 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Hepatic involvement of <b>histoplasmosis </b>is usually secondary to spread from {{c1::pulmonary}} histoplasmosis. <div><div>{{c1::Hepatic::Organ}} infection with <i>Pneumocystis jirovecii </i>is classically secondary to the <u>use of inhaled pentamidine</u> to treat pulmonary Pneumocystis pneumonia in an immunocompromised patient, as pentamidine is <u>not absorbed systemically</u> and thus would <u>not prevent</u> {{c1::hepatic::organ}} infection.<br></div></div>	Hepatic Pneumocystis jiroveci is seen in disseminated disease in the severely immunocompromised. <div>The <b>{{c1::Milan}} criteria</b> is used to assess <u>appropriateness of liver transplantation</u> in those with HCC or cirrhosis. To be considered for orthotopic liver transplantation, one must have:</div><div><br><div><ol><li>Single tumor {{c2::&lt;5 cm::criteria}} or {{c2::up to three tumors, each with diameter &lt;3 cm::multiple tumor criteria}}.</li><li>No {{c3::extrahepatic}} involvement.</li><li>No {{c2::major vascular}} involvement.</li></ol></div></div>				"<img src=""816f5eff26bab04de722e50076e98999.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Transplant	d48da0e5-6f13-4ad0-818c-122802fd3b97	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0121 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Normal <b>liver transplant post-op</b> findings may include:</div><br><div><ul><li>Periportal {{c1::edema}}</li><li>Minimal {{c2::ascites}}</li><li>Right-sided {{c3::pleural effusion}}</li><li>Small perihepatic {{c4::hematoma}}</li></ul></div>				"<img src=""816f5eff26bab04de722e50076e98999.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Liver Transplant	8cb1e586-c8b0-46fc-9f6d-d6e3839e5f1e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0121 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Liver Transplant Complications</u></div><div><br><b>Vascular</b>: <b>{{c1::Hepatic artery thrombosis}}</b> is the most common vascular complication.</div><br><div>Others include hepatic artery {{c2::stenosis}}, IVC/hepatic vein/portal vein {{c3::stenosis}} or {{c3::thrombosis}} and {{c4::pseudoaneurysm}}<br></div>	Other complications include hematoma, abscess, hepatitis, splenic infarct, recurrent malignancy or primary sclerosing cholangitis (depending on the indication for transplant) and post-transplant lymphoproliferative disorder (PTLD). <div><u>Liver Transplant Complications</u></div><div><br>Biliary: <b>{{c1::Ductal stricture}}</b> is the most common biliary complication.</div><br><div>Leaks and obstruction due to {{c2::choledocholithiasis}} are also possible<br></div>	Other complications include hematoma, abscess, hepatitis, splenic infarct, recurrent malignancy or primary sclerosing cholangitis (depending on the indication for transplant) and post-transplant lymphoproliferative disorder (PTLD). <div><b>Budd-Chiari syndrome</b> is {{c1::hepatic venous outflow obstruction}}, which can be thrombotic or non-thrombotic.&nbsp;<br></div>				"<img src=""816f5eff26bab04de722e50076e98999.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Vascular Liver Disease	700512f1-c069-4882-b99f-e3ec97cc9af3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0121 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::01_Liver Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><u>Veno-occlusive Disease of the Liver</u></div><div>Differential diagnosis in patients after <u>stem cell transplant</u> includes {{c1::graft-versus-host disease <br>(GVHD)}}.&nbsp;<br></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	21f3fccf-9e76-481f-84a8-9493ddb326eb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><u>Veno-occlusive Disease of the Liver</u></div><div>Veno-occlusive disease is more likely than GVHD if the {{c1::right hepatic vein}} diameter is &lt;{{c2::0.45}} cm while GVHD is more likely if there is associated {{c3::small bowel wall thickening}}.<br></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	80c9d88f-4049-4f55-90b3-85bc6f144aa0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Peliosis hepatis}} is a rare benign disorder of {{c2::sinusoidal}} dilatation and formation of {{c2::blood- filled lacunae}}.<br></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	39c42483-841f-46d3-a702-69259a46c885	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Peliosis hepatis is often idiopathic but may occur due to certain&nbsp;</div><div><ol><li>{{c1::medications (including steroids, oral contraceptives, tamoxifen and methotrexate)}},</li><li>&nbsp;{{c1::immune disorders (including HIV, immunosuppression post-transplant)}} and&nbsp;</li><li>{{c1::infections (including HIV, TB, Bartonella).::x3 broad categories}}</li></ol></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	29ecf60f-80ee-48f7-a04a-a5cdcd53a9ae	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>CT and MRI in Peliosis hepatis show early {{c1::central}} enhancement with delayed {{c1::centrifugal}} enhancement. Ultrasound may show a non-specific {{c2::hyper}}echoic mass.</div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	b10d50a8-32e8-424a-a241-57f65d2b5e26	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Cardiac hepatopathy}} is passive hepatic congestion from cardiac surgery, heart failure, constrictive pericarditis, or right-sided valvular disease, which may ultimately lead to {{c2::cirrhosis}}.<br></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	414341b5-6cd8-4ba5-a070-07d7a3600cd8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Imaging findings in <b>cardiac hepatopathy </b>include&nbsp;</div><div><ol><li>enlarged {{c1::hepatic veins}} and {{c1::IVC}},&nbsp;</li><li>with {{c4::reflux of intravenous contrast from the right atrium into the {{c1::IVC}} and {{c1::hepatic veins}}.}}&nbsp;</li><li>The liver is typically enlarged and&nbsp;</li><li>demonstrates mottled enhancement ({{c2::nutmeg}} liver).&nbsp;</li><li>{{c3::Ascites::other abdominal finding}} is usually present.</li></ol></div>				"<img src=""8174496ff68acc80de1ef41d540bfdec.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging - Liver - Vascular Liver Disease	058c539f-15ac-45c0-804c-da9dee83f926	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0122 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::02_Hepatic_Doppler Core_Radiology_2E"

A <b>double-contrast esophagram</b> utilizes {{c1::<u>barium</u>}} and {{c1::<u>gas-forming crystals</u>}} to simultaneously <i>distend </i>the esophagus and <i>coat </i>the mucosa with radiopaque contrast. An important long-term sequela of <b>peptic esophagitis</b> is <u>Barrett’s esophagus</u>, which is {{c1::metaplasia}} of normal squamous epithelium to gastric-type adenomatous mucosa.&nbsp;<br>	<span>Barrett’s&nbsp;</span><span>esophagus is a <u>precursor lesion</u> to esophageal adenocarcinoma.</span>			"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"					"<img src=""8f8f79db30514418a4889a8c599d404e.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	4c06aaa5-c33e-4995-b45a-b862b8888f31	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Barrett’s&nbsp;esophagus </b>is a precursor lesion to {{c1::esophageal adenocarcinoma}}.<br></div>				"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"					"<img src=""8f8f79db30514418a4889a8c599d404e.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	50fd95bc-e604-4731-969e-a2eb33b7676a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Nearly 10% of patients with {{c1::reflux esophagitis::esophageal pathology}} may have some <u>adenomatous metaplasia</u>.<br></div>				"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	53e40192-e2b0-41b1-a7df-c4ca588c2296	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>On double-contrast fluoroscopy, <b>Barrett’s esophagus</b> demonstrates a {{c1::reticular (web-like)}} mucosal pattern, often with a {{c2::segmental stricture}} in the mid-esophagus.<br></div>	"<img src=""d4da3244c72281818f4ad37f200505c1.webp"" style=""width: 494.398px;""><br>Radiopedia:<br>""There is background granularity to the normal smooth-as-glass appearance of the esophagus, compatible with reflux esophagitis.<div>That's not all there is, though... at the gastro-esophageal junction, there is a fine reticular pattern superimposed on the granularity. This pattern is concerning for Barrett esophagus, which this turned out to be on EGD and biopsy.""</div>"			"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"					"<img src=""8f8f79db30514418a4889a8c599d404e.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	fcc25919-4c0d-4549-956b-f5784803c73c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Barrett’s esophagus</b> is often associated with <u>esophageal stricture</u>, which is abnormally {{c1::high::high/low}} in location compared to a peptic stricture.<br></div>				"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"					"<img src=""8f8f79db30514418a4889a8c599d404e.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	01da2efd-b098-4c7f-a913-d58805e6d694	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Although radiographic distinction between types of <b>infectious esphagitis </b>has been described, {{c1::endoscopy::procedure}} and subsequent {{c1::biopsy::procedure}} are typically performed in clinical practice to differentiate.<br></div>				"<img src=""91cbae667c5d2669bdf9e5e30135f0e9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Esophagus: Esophagitis	729ab04e-319c-41b9-be84-6daaada1bf61	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0175 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::06_Esophagus Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::Gastric volvulus}} occurs when the stomach twists on its mesentery by at least 180 degrees and results in bowel obstruction or ischemia.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>The stomach may be partly or entirely above&nbsp;</span><span>the diaphragm.</span>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"					"<img src=""28a36f88199ec8e1e8dc6739083b92c6.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Hiatal Hernias	90d4dda7-efc9-4340-88e4-185a1427c73d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>If the stomach is twisted but <u>without</u> obstruction or ischemia, it is referred to as gastric “{{c1::rotation}}.”<br></div>	<div>Vs volvulus&nbsp;</div>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Hiatal Hernias	e89d98e5-1a96-4689-a517-8d546f94f004	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Organoaxial}} rotation/volvulus is when the stomach rotates on its <u>long</u>-axis.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"					"<img src=""28a36f88199ec8e1e8dc6739083b92c6.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Hiatal Hernias	cbb857d0-05da-4d8c-9b7a-fb035e5b6187	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Mesenteroaxial}} rotation/volvulus is when the stomach rotates on its <u>short</u>-axis.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Hiatal Hernias	e84e17eb-80b1-41bf-846d-214a00f3a464	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Gastric volvulus</b> most commonly occurs in the setting of a {{c1::paraesophageal hernia}} or {{c1::trauma}}.<br></div>	"<div><img src=""b42166766f86ff9c17dd7b30867739de.webp""><br></div><div><i>Fundamentals of Body CT</i></div>"			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp""><i></i>"					"<img src=""28a36f88199ec8e1e8dc6739083b92c6.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Hiatal Hernias	a2796031-50ca-44f5-97be-75f154c29f50	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>Axial/Coronal Oral C+ CT</div><div><img src=""0ffc8851cefa9fed2a2ba2a9f08da4c6.webp"" style=""width: 633.883px;""><img src=""748b955e8dc2514992b8460ffc7bc224.webp"" style=""width: 651.242px;""><br></div><br><div><span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">Yellow&nbsp;⇉</span>: Distal stomach located in chest through large hiatal hernia</div><div><span style=""color: rgb(210, 35, 41);"">Red&nbsp;→</span>: Gastroduodenal junction</div><div><span style=""color: rgb(0, 174, 239);"">Blue&nbsp;→</span>: Gastroesophageal junction</div><div>Diagnosis:&nbsp;{{c1::Gastric volvulus (mesenteroaxial)}}</div>"	<div>The gastroduodenal junction appears to be cranial to the gastroesophageal junction. <div><b>Thickened gastric folds</b> are most commonly due to {{c1::<u>inflammatory gastritis</u>}}, which characteristically produces {{c2::smooth::description}} fold thickening.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	90732b77-437e-426d-b71d-c7c4ab10ef9a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Nodular gastric fold thickening</b> is suggestive of {{c1::neoplasm}}<br></div>	<div>Either gastric lymphoma or submucosal&nbsp;carcinoma (which may be primary gastric or metastatic).<br></div>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"					"<img src=""c63c5209cef74d7bef00d18ec2c9d107.webp""><img src=""231b72763903b75461e7e161580ef772.webp""><img src=""42cf58151536c62f9fff24ae667b92b8.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	2fc34810-6786-4aec-9bb2-1a5377b3822b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>Contrast filling {{c1::thickened gastric folds::structures}} (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;⇉</span>) on a double contrast barium study, thought to&nbsp;represent gastritis in this patient.<br></div><br><div><img src=""8338470c34d35d94cb739e014f621f3e.webp"" style=""width: 615.219px;""><br></div>"	<br>			"<img src=""aade03f54d32e7bb4f3251bd768986ac.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	541f1d08-0ef9-4483-b8a3-919f0af5cee0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0187 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
{{c1::Helicobacter pylori::Bacteria}} is a major cause of gastritis, gastric ulcers, and duodenal ulcers.				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""c10837ecb2e16105bfddbab9f3199b0c.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	db357c4b-c144-4e0d-98b1-b612a6267698	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Zollinger-Ellison (ZES)}} syndrome</b> is gastrin over-production from a <u>gastrinoma</u>, which is a neuroendocrine tumor located in the duodenum or pancreas that has a 50% rate of malignancy.&nbsp;	ZE features elevated gastrin level and a paradoxical increase in gastrin after&nbsp;secretin administration.			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""98a6bff7b12b9cf8a34dd7258547ed93.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	b37508f9-46a0-4b4b-b174-4989ecf14db7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Zollinger-Ellison syndrome</b> features elevated gastrin level and a <i>paradoxical</i> increase in gastrin after&nbsp;{{c1::secretin}} administration.	Normally, Secretin helps regulate the&nbsp;pH&nbsp;of the duodenum by <b>inhibiting </b>the secretion of&nbsp;gastric acid&nbsp;from the&nbsp;parietal cells&nbsp;of the stomach and stimulating the production of&nbsp;bicarbonate&nbsp;from the&nbsp;ductal cells&nbsp;of the pancreas.&nbsp;It also stimulates the secretion of bicarbonate and water by&nbsp;cholangiocytes&nbsp;in the bile duct, protecting it from&nbsp;bile acids&nbsp;by controlling the pH and promoting the flow in the duct.			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""98a6bff7b12b9cf8a34dd7258547ed93.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	ffb4838e-b6cc-4de0-b0c9-357c781c46d1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
25% of patients with <b>gastrinoma</b> have {{c1::multiple endocrine neoplasia (MEN) type 1::syndrome}}.	MEN-1 consists of parathyroid adenoma, pituitary adenoma, and pancreatic islet cell tumors.			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	3f511719-fe7b-4139-a97f-56b554cc76d3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Eosinophilic}} gastritis</b> is characterized by <u>thickened folds</u> in the stomach and small bowel in a patient with a history of {{c2::atopy}}.				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""02cadcc5a443d6548a59b4c16935d4a3.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	313df8fa-f81f-40d3-9c2e-4f7b123e50bb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>{{c1::Ménétrier disease}} </b>is a <u>protein-losing enteropathy</u> that is often a diagnosis of exclusion.<br><br>It usually affects the proximal stomach and is pathologically characterized by replacement of {{c2::parietal}} cells by {{c2::hyperplastic epithelial}} cells, leading to {{c3::achlorhydria}}.				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""c1aab0ea879b20187ba8c03750a61c3d.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	65b340d4-6823-44c1-bf93-1f13ee242dbb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Ménétrier disease</b> has a controversial association with {{c1::gastric carcinoma}}.				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""c1aab0ea879b20187ba8c03750a61c3d.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	1b1f29e8-ffaf-42d0-958a-84682154fcd7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
The stomach is rarely an isolated site of involvement by <b>Crohn's disease</b>. Usually the {{c1::distal::distal/proximal}} half of the stomach is affected.				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""2e592e0b29861fe248d1bf27211426f0.webp""><img src=""02a5d3e6c5f1ae75659b11fd6edb35f9.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	333f7c30-3fca-489f-9b04-63bdcd696ed7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
Imaging features in <b>Crohn's disease</b> involving the stomach: <br><br><ol><li>{{c3::Thickened}} folds</li><li>{{c2::Mural ulcers}} most commonly affecting the antrum </li><li>Eventual tubular stenosis of the antrum leading to the characteristic {{c1::ram’s horn}} appearance</li></ol>	"Differential diagnosis of the ram’s horn appearance is sarcoid, Crohn’s disease, and treated ulcer disease.<br><br><img src=""9bb0afaa7b965a1c2b25335e84597e1e.webp"" style=""width: 666.234px;""><br><i>Applied Radiology<br></i><br><img src=""6781b0ac370a34fd1f3dbe0cb5f6eccc.webp""><br>Apparently the two look alike"			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""2e592e0b29861fe248d1bf27211426f0.webp""><img src=""02a5d3e6c5f1ae75659b11fd6edb35f9.webp""><img src=""b8b460bc816718d45f294463abf1004a.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	7433751e-2673-49de-8904-267ecce6b6af	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<b>Gastric varices</b> (from portal hypertension), sarcoidosis, gastric lymphoma, and submucosal carcinoma are <u>non-inflammatory</u> causes of {{c1::thickened}} gastric folds.	<i>versus H. pylori, ZES, eosinophilic gastritis, Crohn's disease which are <u>inflammatory</u></i>			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""66eb88d52f9e4424728870923e478239.webp""><img src=""fd39124c413495c9a136d4e74fad0140.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Thickened Gastric Folds	dbd29255-b274-4046-98d9-f4806e76c82d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
A <b>{{c1::hyperplastic}} polyp</b>, also known as an <b>{{c1::inflammatory}} polyp</b>, is a cystic dilation of a gastric gland that develops in response to chronic inflammation, often associated with {{c2::<i>H. pylori </i>infection::eitology}}.&nbsp;	Hyperplastic polyps are almost always benign, with very rare cases of malignant&nbsp;transformation having been reported.			"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""fb256703fa5b3ac30f59f2fa665b3f27.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Gastric Polyps	c8ec2c6d-fe06-4ec4-8415-38672268bcb7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div><div><div>Double-Contrast Barium Study: A few small, round,&nbsp;well-circumscribed radiolucent&nbsp;filling defects (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;⇉</span>) within the&nbsp;greater curvature of the stomach</div></div><br><div>Likely diagnosis:&nbsp;{{c1::gastric polyps}}</div></div><br><div><img src=""f20679fe8d41e580b359d44d12347096.webp"" style=""width: 722.125px;""><br></div></div>"				"<img src=""59a67a8d0485f725efae0d5a86870f51.webp"">"					"<img src=""fb256703fa5b3ac30f59f2fa665b3f27.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Gastric Polyps	e38710f1-e0a7-448e-a201-22faf45aac21	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>{{c1::Fundic gland}} polyps </b>are associated with {{c2::proton pump inhibitor::medication}} use, but may also occur in</div><div>polyposis syndromes such as {{c3::familial adenomatous polyposis (FAP)}}.&nbsp;</div></div>	<div>Fundic gland polyps have a rare malignant potential, which is more common in patients with FAP.</div>			"<img src=""e9734f2f6f68c2e6dc83b167ea01c2ed.webp"">"					"<img src=""8826fa3cf0550e326ce41cd4c1a9a4a7.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Gastric Polyps	d24a9f45-0121-4d2b-9ab1-9c194c0bfe3c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0188 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>An {{c1::adenomatous}} polyp is a neoplastic polyp with potential of malignant transformation to adenocarcinoma&nbsp;<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""e9734f2f6f68c2e6dc83b167ea01c2ed.webp"">"					"<img src=""fb256703fa5b3ac30f59f2fa665b3f27.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Gastric Polyps	0f756d28-22f2-4784-a46a-4195e6bb93f9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0189 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Risk factors for <u>malignant transformation</u> of <b>adenomatous polyp</b> to adenocarcinoma:</div><br><div><ol><li>{{c1::Increased size::Factors}}</li><li>{{c1::Villous contour}}&nbsp;</li><li>{{c1::Presence of cellular dysplasia}}</li></ol></div>	<br>			"<img src=""e9734f2f6f68c2e6dc83b167ea01c2ed.webp"">"					"<img src=""fb256703fa5b3ac30f59f2fa665b3f27.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Gastric Polyps	fc86cd86-a866-4a10-9c1d-5aeb31b12cf1	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0189 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::Gastrointestinal stromal tumor (GIST)}} is the most common <u>submucosal gastric tumor</u> and may be benign or malignant.&nbsp;<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5197259801766e52b5ca6a4eb0aeb887.webp"">"					"<img src=""67fbb730bc6df9ffd855c1ce6438535d.webp""><img src=""f67adc6429618efb1f1c7806e04881be.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Benign Gastric Masses	ecd43e2f-c3ea-4227-8e4e-e5bfddf4a884	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0190 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>While <b>GIST</b> may occur anywhere in the GI tract, the {{c1::stomach}} is the most common location.&nbsp;</div><br><div>The tumor arises from the {{c2::interstitial cells of Cajal::cells}}, which are pacemaker cells that drive peristalsis.<br></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5197259801766e52b5ca6a4eb0aeb887.webp"">"					"<img src=""67fbb730bc6df9ffd855c1ce6438535d.webp""><img src=""f67adc6429618efb1f1c7806e04881be.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Benign Gastric Masses	d9f0442e-a5d2-4c17-94d1-c6615e69bae3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0190 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>Major risk factors for&nbsp;<b>gastric cancer&nbsp;</b>are conditions that cause&nbsp;{{c1::chronic inflammation}}:</div><br><div><ol><li>Ingestion of polycyclic hydrocarbons and nitrosamines (from processed meats)</li><li>Atrophic gastritis</li><li>Pernicious anemia</li><li>Post-subtotal gastrectomy</li></ol></div>	<br>			"<img src=""ae1c651699d2aa4060f5c4b54f05895a.webp"">"					"<img src=""98f47b90856ba080e25c3b68ce1ec09a.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Malignant Gastric Masses	020d5bbd-ce98-4d21-b15c-0daf146cd2cd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0191 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>Lymphatic spread of <b>gastric adenocarcinoma&nbsp;</b>occurs along:</div><br><div>the {{c1::lesser curvature}}&nbsp;<b>→</b>&nbsp;the {{c2::gastrohepatic ligament}} → liver</div><div>and the {{c1::greater curvature}} → the {{c2::gastrocolic ligament}} → peritoneum<br></div>	"<div>most common sites of metastasis are liver (in 48% of metastatic cancer patients), peritoneum (32%), lung (15%), and bone (12%)<br></div><br><div><img src=""570bb5479ab1c9d49f440c1449f33615.webp""><br></div><div><i>doi:10.1148/rg.2019180113</i><br></div><br><div><i>this is not stated as plainly in Core, but can be read in the paper above</i></div>"			"<img src=""ae1c651699d2aa4060f5c4b54f05895a.webp"">"					"<img src=""98f47b90856ba080e25c3b68ce1ec09a.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Malignant Gastric Masses	20ffccb3-7e2f-4628-92e0-4c1e77d26b72	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0191 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
