<div><div><u>Roux-en-Y Anatomy</u><br></div><br><div>The <b>{{c2::Roux}} limb</b> is created by transecting the jejunum approximately 35–45 cm distal to the ligament of Treitz, then bringing it up to be anastomosed to the {{c1::gastric pouch}} via a narrow gastrojejunostomy stoma.<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5ab7320a25c2ec785274c75760d2fdff.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Overview of Common Gastric Surgeries	9a683b58-cc25-4fac-bc95-ac285696e4a9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0194 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Roux-en-Y Anatomy</u><br></div><br><div>The current favored approach for placement of the<b> Roux limb</b> relative to the colon is {{c1::antecolic (in front of the transverse colon)}}.&nbsp;<br></div></div>	<div>The Roux limb used to be placed retrocolic, which required the creation&nbsp;of a surgical defect through the transverse mesocolon (mesentery of the transverse colon).&nbsp;A retrocolic Roux limb has a higher risk of a transmesocolic hernia due to the defect in the&nbsp;transverse mesocolon.<br></div>			"<img src=""5ab7320a25c2ec785274c75760d2fdff.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Overview of Common Gastric Surgeries	a873d4a3-e88b-421f-9b37-866530021046	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0194 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><u>Roux-en-Y Anatomy</u><br></div><br><div>The RYGB leads to <b>weight loss</b> both from {{c1::early satiety}} (due to small size of the gastric pouch) and {{c1::malabsorption}} (due to surgical bypass of the proximal jejunum).<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""5ab7320a25c2ec785274c75760d2fdff.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Overview of Common Gastric Surgeries	d87ceeef-2143-4a47-b850-ed3fa9631976	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0194 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Postoperative leak</b> is usually diagnosed by {{c1::10}} days after surgery.<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	dd733a28-3622-4b8f-84ab-9320cba5c122	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>An {{c1::upper GI}} study with {{c1::water-soluble}} contrast is the study of choice if a <u>leak</u> is suspected.<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	8932f2cf-3a1a-4baf-8d3b-586f81b82eea	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Leaks</b> may arise from the {{c1::gastric pouch}} or {{c1::blind-ending jejunal limb}}.&nbsp;<br></div><br><div>It is rare for a leak to arise from the distal jejunojejunostomy.<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	db9500bb-5c94-46f8-b795-8d5b7cfe29b6	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div><img src=""ce3efcb303cf007129bade95fc6c889b.webp""><br></div><br><div>Single contrast upper GI study in a patient status post RYGB shows prompt contrast filling of the {{c1::excluded stomach}} (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;→</span>) via a {{c1::gastrogastric fistula}} at the superior aspect of the gastric suture line <span style=""color: rgb(210, 35, 41);"">red&nbsp;→</span>.<br></div></div>"	<div>A gastrogastric fistula is a communication between the gastric pouch and the excluded&nbsp;stomach, which may be an early or late complication of RYGB. Imaging findings include gas&nbsp;and fluid (or enteric contrast, if given) within the excluded stomach on CT or upper GI study.<br></div>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	c7599887-8eb9-4dc1-bc25-21f74934d1fd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div><img src=""ce3efcb303cf007129bade95fc6c889b.webp"" style=""width: 764.898px;""></div><br><div>A {{c1::gastrogastric fistula}} may be a cause of <u>inadequate weight loss</u> or <u>recurrent weight gain</u>.<br></div></div>"	"<div>Single contrast upper Gl study in a patient status post Roux-en-Y gastric bypass shows prompt contrast filling of the excluded stomach (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;→</span>) via a gastrogastric fistula at the superior aspect of the gastric suture line ((<span style=""color: rgb(210, 35, 41);"">red&nbsp;→</span>)).<br></div>"			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	4bd616e1-f31f-4340-856f-391007c97c57	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Early SBO</b> in the acute postoperative period is most often due to {{c1::edema}} or {{c1::hematoma}} at the gastrojejunostomy or jejunojejunostomy.<br></div></div>	<div>Treatment is usually conservative, with most cases resolving as the edema and/or hematoma resolves.<br></div>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	d3a32b2c-ca77-4509-80ca-ce2e5dc8b7da	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>With a <b>retrocolic Roux limb</b>, <u>edema</u> at the {{c1::transverse mesocolon}} defect may also cause early SBO.&nbsp;<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	d81ae080-434c-4982-88b5-478ed92e95cf	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Late presentation of <b>SBO</b> may be due to {{c1::internal hernia::complication}} (more common with laparoscopic surgery) or {{c1::adhesions::complication}} (more common with open surgery).<br></div></div>	"<div><div><img alt=""Two similar cases of internal hernia after laparoscopic Roux-en-Y gastric  bypass surgery | BMJ Case Reports"" src=""6261b55b309980ba3863ce5a653f80ec.webp""><br></div><br></div>"			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	034b08ba-c2b9-42de-bbd9-1967fa8c311e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Intermittent partial or complete <u>mechanical obstruction of the afferent limb</u> is seen in up to 13% of patients both in acute (&lt;7 days postoperative) or chronic (&gt;7 days postoperative) phase.<br></div><br><div>This is referred to as&nbsp;{{c1::afferent loop syndrome}}.</div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"					"<img src=""b4835b9911753d9dc8a892149eed1a20.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	06cf0053-bde2-4c38-a784-7e8631b038b4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div><div>Fluoroscopy cannot diagnosis <b>afferent loop syndrome</b>, as the afferent limb does not usually opacify with contrast (unless there is reflux from the jejunojejunostomy).&nbsp;<br></div><br><div>CT would show&nbsp;<span style=""text-align: left;"">{{c1::dilated, fluid-filled afferent/pancreaticobiliary limb}}.</span><br></div></div>"	<br>			"<img src=""783d1d6bdba5855c732fbd6009cbf69f.webp"">"					"<img src=""b4835b9911753d9dc8a892149eed1a20.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	2676a04b-5e13-4693-8819-ee44f6123ef8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0195 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><i>Laparoscopic</i> Roux-en-Y procedures are associated with a higher rate of {{c1::internal hernias}}<br></div><div>(seen in 2.5% of laparoscopic procedures) compared to open procedures (0.5%).&nbsp;<br></div></div>	<div>Internal hernias can be difficult to diagnose, both clinically and by imaging.<br></div>			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	ff458e05-a1e2-4821-8f45-f198021892df	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>{{c1::Internal hernias}} usually present within two years of bypass and are the <u>most common cause of SBO</u><b> </b>after a <i>laparoscopic</i><b> </b>Roux-en-Y.<br></div></div>	"<div><img alt=""Two similar cases of internal hernia after laparoscopic Roux-en-Y gastric  bypass surgery | BMJ Case Reports"" src=""6261b55b309980ba3863ce5a653f80ec.webp""><br></div><br>"			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	70b750bc-d7a9-4dc8-a4b4-f5365b6d82df	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Internal hernias</b> may also present as mesenteric and bowel {{c1::edema}} without obstruction.<br></div></div>				"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	d49c237c-99c9-41b7-82f1-4039f376530b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>Characteristic locations of <b>Roux-en-Y gastric bypass-associated internal hernias</b>:</div><br><div><ol><li>{{c1::Transmesocolic}} hernia (associated with a retrocolic Roux limb)</li><li>{{c2::Peterson's}} space (between the mesentery of the Roux limb and the transverse mesocolon)<br></li><li>Mesenteric defect created by the&nbsp;{{c3::jejunojejunostomy}}<br></li></ol></div></div>	"<div><img alt=""Two similar cases of internal hernia after laparoscopic Roux-en-Y gastric  bypass surgery | BMJ Case Reports"" src=""6261b55b309980ba3863ce5a653f80ec.webp""><br></div><br><div>Imaging features of internal hernia include swirling of the mesentery, a mushroom shape</div><div>of the mesentery, and/or the presence of small bowel loops posterior to the superior</div><div>mesenteric artery.</div>"			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	4650a6f9-216f-4781-aae2-a421e82f7631	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>narrowing of the {{c1::gastrojejunostomy stoma}} may occur in up to 10% of patients, leading to <u>dilation</u> of the gastric pouch and distal esophagus.&nbsp;<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	7263863b-7e87-4c27-a06e-ff37b4208fc0	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div><b>Stomal stenosis</b> is usually treated with {{c1::endoscopic dilation}}.<br></div></div>	<div>narrowing of the distal jejunojejunostomy is less common and usually requires surgery.<br></div>			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	c2f853d3-0d1d-4c93-8479-8ece90385ccb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>The jejunal mucosa adjacent to the gastrojejunal anastomosis is susceptible to <b>gastric secretions</b>, which can cause {{c1::marginal ulcers}} in up to 3% of patients.<br></div></div>	<br>			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"					"<img src=""1d067998cf889fcef5867c1d01a72a06.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	4e449226-3cf6-4ade-80b4-73367ed2b17e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><div>A <b>marginal ulcer</b> is diagnosed by upper GI as a {{c1::thickening}} and small {{c1::outpouching}} of a gastric fold.<br></div></div>	<div>Treatment is conservative.<br></div>			"<img src=""802c582a2e4e157ab02bc862f93b79f9.webp"">"					"<img src=""1d067998cf889fcef5867c1d01a72a06.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Stomach: Complications of Roux-en-Y Surgery	7c6d92ce-d29e-496f-8190-001e476c8b9d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0196 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::07_Stomach Core_Radiology_2E"
The <b>duodenum</b> has 4 parts: <br><br><ol><li>{{c1::Superior}} (D1)</li><li>{{c1::Descending}} (D2)</li><li>{{c1::Horizontal/transverse}} (D3)</li><li>{{c1::Ascending}} (D4)</li></ol>	"<img src=""878d95c21ed3fb82dcc4dae523e65eb2.webp""><img src=""55f618aad4b02243428fb40c51cba484.webp""><br><span style=""font-weight: 700;"">Figure 1b.</span>&nbsp;Duodenal anatomy. Drawing&nbsp;<b>(a)</b>&nbsp;and coronal CT image&nbsp;<b>(b)</b>&nbsp;show the anatomic relationships of the duodenum: stomach (black *), first segment of the duodenum (<span style=""color: rgb(64, 173, 73);"">green&nbsp;→</span>; green area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), second segment of the duodenum (pink →; pink area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), third segment of the duodenum (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;→</span>; yellow area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), fourth segment of the duodenum (orange&nbsp;→; orange area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), gallbladder (brown * and brown area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), pancreas (brown&nbsp;→), aorta (white * and red area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>), and inferior vena cava (IVC) (blue * and blue area in&nbsp;<b>a</b>).<br><br><a href=""https://pubs.rsna.org/doi/full/10.1148/rg.2020200045"">Imaging Spectrum of Duodenal Emergencies | RadioGraphics (rsna.org)</a>"			"<img src=""6febaf6c267a60490066ea7010ae6c12.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Anatomy	9bdcdc73-eb0d-45f3-b8fa-ef2816f95a94	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0197 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
A common <b>small bowel mesentery</b> anchors the <u>jejunum</u> and <u>ileum</u> to the {{c1::posterior abdominal wall::structure}}.	"<img src=""07b92710ec8b12c7aa0f6904285668d3.webp"">"			"<img src=""6febaf6c267a60490066ea7010ae6c12.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Anatomy	6dabd89b-92ff-40dc-9431-0d802b5c5855	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0197 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::Closed-loop obstruction}}&nbsp;represents obstruction of both the <i>efferent</i> and <i>afferent</i> segments of a single loop of bowel and is a <u>surgical emergency</u> due to risk of bowel ischemia.&nbsp;<br></div>				"<img src=""db64c5400c9814b332912046141ea438.webp"">"					"<img src=""db9738d21ffac400e5eded2ca7827a15.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	89fccc34-efed-4718-9737-723708a1383c	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0199 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Closed-loop obstruction </b>is almost always seen in association with {{c1::small&nbsp;bowel volvulus}}, which may be due to adhesions or internal hernia.<br></div>				"<img src=""db64c5400c9814b332912046141ea438.webp"">"					"<img src=""db9738d21ffac400e5eded2ca7827a15.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	be4a7931-9d51-4a1a-a60f-b7e2b59cb293	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0199 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>CT imaging features of <b>closed-loop obstruction</b>:</div><br><div><ol><li>The {{c1::<u>whirl</u>}}<u> sign</u> due to twisting of mesenteric vessels seen in volvulus.&nbsp;</li><li>{{c2::<u>U</u>}}<u>- or </u>{{c2::<u>C</u>}}<u>-shaped</u> distribution of the distended bowel loops with radially oriented vessels.&nbsp;</li><li><u>Mesenteric </u>{{c3::<u>edema</u>}} is often present.</li></ol></div>	"<img src=""9810a48490210e70fde020ceb5d54d73.webp"">"			"<img src=""db64c5400c9814b332912046141ea438.webp"">"					"<img src=""db9738d21ffac400e5eded2ca7827a15.webp""><img src=""785dac3b39631f775cf2f08ad72e5637.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	41dcb62c-3b0f-4113-84c0-40417d2a41da	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0199 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>C+ CT of the abdomen</div><div><img src=""16d075fbeafa3e2bd92c873a26287a19.webp"" style=""width: 630.289px;""><img src=""114162e1b5c599f603cb1da278f88f8d.webp"" style=""width: 576.523px;""><br></div><div>Multiple dilated, fluid-filled loops of small bowel.&nbsp;</div><div>Transition point in the midline pelvis (<span style=""color: rgb(255, 242, 0);"">yellow&nbsp;⇉</span>) with <i>no obstructing mass or evidence of hernia or any other visible causes of obstruction</i>.</div><br><div>Likely cause of obstruction:&nbsp;{{c1::Adhesions}}</div>"	Adhesions are an imaging diagnosis of exclusion as they are not directly visualized by&nbsp;imaging. <br>On CT, a transition point is seen, but no alternative cause for the transition (e.g., no&nbsp;mass or hernia, etc.) is identified. <div>{{c1::Adhesions}} from prior surgery or intra-peritoneal inflammatory process are the <u>most common cause</u> of <b>SBO</b>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>The vast majority of patients with SBO due to adhesions have had&nbsp;</span><span>prior abdominal surgery.</span>			"<img src=""db64c5400c9814b332912046141ea438.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	039c9fb4-a631-408e-b87b-5ca7fbde4cff	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0199 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Adhesions}} are an imaging diagnosis of exclusion as they are not directly visualized by imaging.&nbsp;</div><br><div>On CT, a transition point is seen, but no alternative cause for the transition (e.g., no mass or hernia, etc.) is identified.<br></div>				"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	deb14d21-e5bb-4ba9-858f-fe6d45248073	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>In the <i>absence</i> of signs of <i>impending ischemia</i>, obtructions due to adhesions are usually managed {{c1::non-operatively::surgically or non-operatively}}.<br></div>	<span>&nbsp;with nasogastric tube decompression and bowel rest</span>			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	2cd81f3c-4344-44c2-9bb1-a8135a90a007	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Protrusion of bowel through an abdominal wall defect (hernia)}} is the second most common cause of SBO.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>Approximately 75% of external hernias occur in the groin, with the majority being&nbsp;</span><span>inguinal hernias.</span>			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	4a460b63-2647-4b33-8b52-6d831fc1d240	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>The term {{c2::<b>strangulation</b>}} refers to {{c1::ischemia due to vascular compromise}} by the hernia.<br></div>				"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	60beaa0c-7aee-4b37-be43-b7485a1e79b8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The term {{c1::<b>incarceration</b>}} refers to a hernia that cannot be reduced and is a <u>physical exam finding</u>, not an imaging finding.<br></div>				"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"					"<img src=""5189923514591a968e13595180a20581.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging:&nbsp;Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	8efee425-00db-4702-bedf-308da90769c8	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>An <b>inguinal hernia</b> may be either <u>indirect</u> or <u>direct</u>, depending on the relation of the hernia to the {{c1::inferior epigastric vessels}}.<br></div>	"<img src=""002371e5e5de1581218fa7aede9b8d29.webp""><br><img src=""59228190d1352d46f519358a93ea97a7.webp""><br><i>(Radiographics&nbsp;</i>Diagnosis of Inguinal Region Hernias with Axial CT: The Lateral Crescent Sign and Other Key Findings)"			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	66d3c8c1-2524-4ce3-99a1-0b833b429b74	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>{{c1::Indirect::direct/indirect}} inguinal hernia</b> is the <u>most common type</u> and is more common in <u>males</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>	"<img src=""a7a99515cc28f46d38bed427ddfd5289.webp"" style=""width: 643.188px;""><i>&nbsp;<img src=""0713fbf41479a987f84ce8181aa437d0.webp"" style=""width: 494.398px;""><br>RadioGraphics</i>"			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	8f8b1277-06f0-4934-bb5f-25a523bd64a7	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>In <b>indirect inguinal hernias</b>, the neck of&nbsp;the hernia is {{c1::lateral::lateral/medial}} to the inferior epigastric vessels.</div><br><div>Hernia contents travel with the {{c2::spermatic cord}},&nbsp;often into the scrotum.&nbsp;<br></div>	"<br><i>2 examples from radiographics:<br><img src=""a7a99515cc28f46d38bed427ddfd5289.webp""><br><img src=""0713fbf41479a987f84ce8181aa437d0.webp""><br>In males, the inguinal canal transmits the spermatic cord to the scrotum. The spermatic cord is covered by the fascia&nbsp;</i>from all three abdominal wall muscle aponeuroses and comprises the ductus (vas) deferens, testicular artery and veins (pampiniform plexus), and genital branch of the genitofemoral<br>nerve. The ilioinguinal nerve runs along the front of the spermatic cord. (RadioGraphics: Diagnosis of Inguinal Region Hernias with Axial CT: The Lateral Crescent Sign and Other Key Findings)<br><br>*In females the inguinal canal transmits the round ligament of the uterus and the ilioinguinal nerve to the labia majora." <div>The neck of a <b>direct inguinal hernia</b> is {{c1::medial::medial/lateral}} to the inferior epigastric vessels, protruding through a weak area in the anterior abdominal wall (Hesselbach’s triangle).<br></div>	"<br><i>2 labeled examples:<br><img src=""003580a20e947254d00f98d0908b6990.webp""><br><img src=""582bf1b9ee713251d4f2711de78bc725.webp""><br><br>Anatomy:<br><img src=""002371e5e5de1581218fa7aede9b8d29.webp""><br><img src=""59228190d1352d46f519358a93ea97a7.webp""><br>(Radiographics&nbsp;</i>Diagnosis of Inguinal Region Hernias with Axial CT: The Lateral Crescent Sign and Other Key Findings)"			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	f8971491-a72c-4f82-ba7d-c47b0806dd7e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>{{c1::Direct::Direct/indirect}} inguinal hernias</b> <u>do not</u> go into the scrotum.<br></div>	"<br><i>2 labeled examples:</i><br><img src=""003580a20e947254d00f98d0908b6990.webp""><br><img src=""582bf1b9ee713251d4f2711de78bc725.webp""><br>(RadioGraphics: Diagnosis of Inguinal Region Hernias with Axial CT: The Lateral Crescent Sign and Other Key Findings)"			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	b1e0067a-c200-42a4-8ec5-da76d63265c4	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Direct inguinal hernias</b> are considered <u>acquired</u> and may be caused by increased {{c1::intra-abdominal pressure}}, such&nbsp;as obesity, COPD and chronic constipation.<br></div>	"<img src=""582bf1b9ee713251d4f2711de78bc725.webp""><br><i>(Radiographics&nbsp;</i>Diagnosis of Inguinal Region Hernias with Axial CT: The Lateral Crescent Sign and Other Key Findings)"			"<img src=""44687dba65845357afc04e6ef40401c2.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	04f0baf6-eada-4927-9b2c-d05bf842d602	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0200 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

"<div><b>{{c1::Spigelian}} hernia </b>is a <u>lateral ventral hernia</u> that occurs at the {{c2::<u>semilunar</u>}}<u> line</u> (between the rectus abdominis and lateral oblique muscles).&nbsp;<br></div><br><div><img src=""b2c463e15bb89d7926145ce2d06f0afc.webp""><br></div>"	"<span>Image from radiopaedia: Omental herniation through defect in the transversus abdominis and internal oblique muscles<br><br>It is associated with ipsilateral cryptorchidism&nbsp;</span><span>amongst male infants due to failure of development of a gubernaculum.<br></span><br><img src=""272dd758156961c64e576c43e561411b.webp""><img src=""9211671abe01ad4d4cc7fd707749eaaa.webp"">"			"<img src=""65b27b0a35e07e4ed2e874a7c16f4554.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	240d1c08-df9b-4a58-b207-8496be31196b	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0201 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>{{c1::Spigelian}} hernia </b>is associated with <u>ipsilateral cryptorchidism</u>&nbsp;amongst male infants due to <i>failure of development</i> of a <u>gubernaculum</u>.<br></div>	"<img src=""55eb42027c992e6743af74580db638ab.webp""><br><div><div><div>There is a herniation of a small bowel segment through the abdominal wall with the herniated sac located lateral to the rectus abdominis muscle,&nbsp;along the&nbsp;semilunar line&nbsp;(Spigelian line) through the transversus abdominis aponeurosis (Spigelian fascia).</div></div></div><div><div><br></div></div><a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/cases/spigelian-hernia-7#image-8203962"">Spigelian hernia | Radiology Case | Radiopaedia.org</a><br>"			"<img src=""65b27b0a35e07e4ed2e874a7c16f4554.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	1457fb2d-9a80-4d3c-a519-d15bb8771aa9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0201 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><i>Any hernia</i> can be called a <b>{{c1::Richter}} hernia</b> when only the <u>antimesenteric portion</u> of the bowel wall is herniated.</div><br><div>These hernias are more likely to result in {{c2::strangulation::complication}} than obstruction.<br></div>	"<img src=""6f19e0a0fa82c9600af6d2f0ab573345.webp"">"			"<img src=""65b27b0a35e07e4ed2e874a7c16f4554.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	f3ceedbf-199c-4c2c-b073-ca9bd60de1c3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0201 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><b>{{c1::Transmesenteric}} hernia</b> is a broad category of internal bowel herniation through <u>defects in any of the three true mesenteries</u> (small bowel mesentery, transverse mesocolon, and sigmoid mesentery).<br></div>	"<img src=""05b679c95f4ca44da6a5c9665c67c906.webp"">"			"<img src=""e55179e5a0d66ab050c408b668b520c8.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	2eeeda8b-ad0d-4edb-b9a8-bdc3fdcd48aa	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0202 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The <i>most common</i> type of <b>transmesenteric hernia</b> is the <u>transmesocolic hernia</u> due to a defect in the {{c1::transverse mesocolon (mesentery of the transverse colon)}}.<br></div>	"<img alt=""Two similar cases of internal hernia after laparoscopic Roux-en-Y gastric  bypass surgery | BMJ Case Reports"" src=""6261b55b309980ba3863ce5a653f80ec.webp"">"			"<img src=""e55179e5a0d66ab050c408b668b520c8.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	e52c10fb-ac09-4f77-9f90-a5a02f7267cd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0202 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div><b>Transmesocolic hernia</b> is seen most commonly post {{c1::Roux-en-Y gastric bypass::surgery}} or {{c1::biliary- enteric anastomosis from liver transplant::surgery}}.<br></div>				"<img src=""e55179e5a0d66ab050c408b668b520c8.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	964e5d74-8433-45b1-9886-507086784143	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0202 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>The {{c1::foramen of Winslow}} is the communication between the <u>lesser sac</u> and the <u>greater peritoneal cavity</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>	"AKA Epiploic foramen<br><div>The foramen is eloquently described as the opening to the lesser sac located ""between the two great veins of the abdomen (portal vein and inferior vena cava)""&nbsp;.</div>Radiopaedia"			"<img src=""e55179e5a0d66ab050c408b668b520c8.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	e104749f-4dec-490c-a1fe-1bec5bf345f5	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0203 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>The key imaging features of a <b>foramen of Winslow hernia</b> are dilated loops of bowel in the {{c1::lesser sac}} and presence of mesentery and/or bowel loops between the {{c2::IVC}} and {{c2::main portal vein}}.<br></div>	"<img src=""f82f46255f9dc5ddc26bb26b487d53b1.webp""><br><img src=""2a2b1c26687f7e5d7a2b2f582b616249.webp""><br><i>Radiopaedia, lesser sac hernia</i>"	"<a href=""https://radiopaedia.org/cases/foramen-of-winslowlesser-sac-internal-hernia-containing-cecum-and-terminal-ileum#image-53974906"">Foramen of Winslow/lesser sac internal hernia containing caecum and terminal ileum | Radiology Case | Radiopaedia.org</a><br>Another interesting case"		"<img src=""e55179e5a0d66ab050c408b668b520c8.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	aed4c42a-f7b4-4735-a706-82cb4b9f9fdd	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0203 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>A mass {{c1::intrinsic}} to the bowel,</div><div>or compression from an {{c1::extrinsic}} mass may cause <b>SBO</b>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>An&nbsp;</span><span>extrinsic mass is usually straightforward to diagnose by CT.</span>			"<img src=""cc030f28f0a3a019e28989afecaefd36.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Small Bowel Obstruction (SBO)	fef7c59a-022a-4445-9c48-2fca0e402d8d	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0203 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>Three phenotypes of <b>Crohn's disease</b>:</div><br><div><ol><li>{{c1::Active inflammation}}: Mural hyperenhancement, intramural edema, mural ulcerations.</li><li>{{c2::Stricturing disease}}: Luminal narrowing with upstream dilatation.</li><li>{{c3::Penetrating disease}}*: Sinus tracts, simple fistulas, complex fistulas, inflammatory mass, abscess.</li></ol></div>	<i>Each phenotype may exist independently or may coexist<br></i><br>*Perianal disease is not considered penetrating disease. <div>CT/MRI findings<b>&nbsp;</b>in&nbsp;<b>Crohn's disease</b><b>:</b><br></div><br><div><b>{{c1::Creeping fat}} </b>describes {{c2::widely separated loops of bowel}} due to fibrofatty proliferation.<br></div>	"The widely separated loops of bowel are also sometimes referred to as ""<b>Proud loop</b>"" sign<br><br><img src=""ce8832ff46f533733df471293cfcd0ac.webp""><br><a href=""https://epos.myesr.org/poster/esr/ecr2016/C-0325"">EPOS™ - C-0325 (myesr.org)</a><br><br>Comb sign describes engorged vasa recta (mesenteric blood vessels) adjacent to an inflamed bowel loop.<br>Pseudosacculation describes the bulging appearance along the antimesenteric border which is spared compared to the fibrotic and shortened mesenteric side.<br><br>Restricted diffusion, when seen with other findings of active inflammation, indicates more severe disease." <div><div>CT/MRI findings<b>&nbsp;</b>in&nbsp;<b>Crohn's disease</b><b>:</b><br></div><br></div><div><div>{{c1::Restricted diffusion::Specific MRI finding}}, when seen with other findings of active inflammation, indicates more severe disease.</div></div>	"<div><ol><li><b>Creeping fat</b> describes widely separated loops of bowel due to fibrofatty proliferation.</li><li><b>Comb sign</b> describes engorged vasa recta (mesenteric blood vessels) adjacent to an inflamed bowel loop.</li><li><b>Pseudosacculation </b>describes the bulging appearance along the antimesenteric border which is spared compared to the fibrotic and shortened mesenteric side.</li><li>Restricted diffusion, when seen with other findings of active inflammation, indicates more severe disease.</li></ol><br>The widely separated loops of bowel are also sometimes referred to as ""<b>Proud loop</b>"" sign<br><div><br><div><img src=""ce8832ff46f533733df471293cfcd0ac.webp""><br></div><div><a href=""https://epos.myesr.org/poster/esr/ecr2016/C-0325"">EPOS™ - C-0325 (myesr.org)</a></div></div></div>"			"<img src=""61825c9d6c256c5cb5641f02d037f24d.webp"">"					"<img src=""c819e7b684c10e2d97fa6b41c46bf4d1.webp""><img src=""94cd56a63231d798880bf9d931713cd6.webp""><img src=""6709a5d5c35e48930872903831c8a7f0.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	43d6272a-e9f8-4cd8-930d-9f355db7ff68	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0205 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>The most characteristic imaging finding of&nbsp;<b>Celiac disease</b>&nbsp;is <i>reversal of </i>{{c1::jejunal and ileal fold patterns}} due to <u>villous atrophy</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>Normally, the jejunum has more and closer together folds compared to the&nbsp;</span><span>ileum. <br><br>However, in celiac disease, the loss of jejunal folds due to villous atrophy causes a&nbsp;</span><span>compensatory increase in the number of ileal folds.</span>			"<img src=""2e5b766b87137d7d9d067025f95f16c8.webp"">"					"<img src=""e5c712f615165af19faf7cede998e159.webp""><img src=""9d5052a6677b9c5976f9aadb62c85ec8.webp""><img src=""6850d5207785a4c730d3af27e95fa2f3.webp""><img src=""33602136dab047ffbf186dc1f781a5d0.webp""><img src=""7ae52756f98ce1113d8376fbbd865563.webp""><img src=""2107d2ae0d1fd6aca23984f9b29652eb.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	03320242-41b9-4f8b-9b14-33259d702cf9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0207 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>An important complication of&nbsp;<b>Celiac disease&nbsp;</b>is<b>&nbsp;</b>{{c1::pneumatosis intestinalis}}, thought to be due to <u>dissection of intraluminal gas through the inflamed bowel wall</u>.&nbsp;<br></div>	<span>Pneumatosis in the setting of celiac disease is <b><u>not</u> thought to reflect bowel ischemia</b></span>			"<img src=""a3d87b44ec5a21312f6cb8c9e2db3f2c.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	bdb70abf-3fd4-4f1e-97d5-20cd22d9ca89	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0208 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
"<div>An important complication of&nbsp;<b>Celiac disease&nbsp;</b>is<b>&nbsp;</b>{{c1::splenic}} atrophy.<br></div><br><div><img src=""03b262e0f395b7a81215e35f2c286939.webp""><br></div>"	<i>Splenic Atrophy in Celiac Disease</i>			"<img src=""a3d87b44ec5a21312f6cb8c9e2db3f2c.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	90bff93b-b9dd-479f-bd0d-387ec980535f	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0208 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>{{c1::<u>Cavitating mesenteric lymph node syndrome (CMLNS)</u>}} is a very rare complication of <u>Celiac disease</u>.<br></div><br><div>The central portion of affected lymph nodes become <u>low attenuation</u> due to <u>liquid necrosis</u>.<br></div>	<span>CMLNS is&nbsp;</span><span>thought to be highly specific for celiac disease when seen in combination with villous atrophy and splenic&nbsp;</span><span>atrophy.<br><br>The differential diagnosis of <u><b>low attenuation mesenteric lymph nodes</b></u> includes: <br><ol><li><span>TB</span></li><li><span>Whipple&nbsp;</span><span>disease</span></li><li><span>treated lymphoma</span></li><li><span>CMLNS</span></li></ol></span><br>			"<img src=""a3d87b44ec5a21312f6cb8c9e2db3f2c.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	d6c4f5bc-4de2-4e02-8857-1ac0c71bfaa9	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0208 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div><b>{{c1::Whipple disease}} </b>is due to infection by <i>{{c2::Tropheryma whipplei}}</i>, which manifests in the GI tract as <u>malabsorption</u><b> </b>and <u>abdominal pain</u>.&nbsp;</div><br><div>May also cause <u>arthralgias</u> and increased <u>skin pigmentation</u>.<br></div>				"<img src=""a3d87b44ec5a21312f6cb8c9e2db3f2c.webp"">"					"<img src=""5a01fecc526c0e659cf46a39750094c8.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	e359eb05-d9b8-4489-976c-3cb3a18fe286	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0208 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
<div>{{c1::Whipple disease}} characteristically causes <u>low attenuation adenopathy</u> that may appear similar to the cavitating mesenteric lymph node syndrome seen in Celiac disease.<br></div>	<span>The differential diagnosis of&nbsp;</span><u><b>low attenuation mesenteric lymph nodes</b></u><span>&nbsp;includes:</span><br><ol><li>TB</li><li>Whipple&nbsp;disease</li><li>treated lymphoma</li><li>CMLNS</li></ol>			"<img src=""a3d87b44ec5a21312f6cb8c9e2db3f2c.webp"">"					"<img src=""5a01fecc526c0e659cf46a39750094c8.webp""><br><i>Mayo Clinic GI Imaging Review</i>"		Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Enteritis	bad01faa-5789-40b6-93a5-64c5ff608d35	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0208 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"

<div>Compared to mucinous neoplasms, {{c1::<u>non-mucinous</u> adenocarcinoma}}&nbsp;of the appendix is much less common.</div><br><div>If seen on imaging, it appears as a <u>soft tissue mass</u>, <u>not associated with a mucocele</u>.<br></div>				"<img src=""dbd508ed0097ee2e96acbb809f4717a6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Small Bowel: Appendix	e0a41454-8bef-4c25-b415-b587ce6e0ded	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0212 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::08_Small_bowel Core_Radiology_2E"
The {{c1::lesser omentum}} connects the <u>liver</u> to the <u>stomach</u>	"<img src=""8c913f5e629520fcd0bb4eb4db8b2088.webp"">"			"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	fd42aaac-b6e7-41da-b405-dbe371368ffc	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The {{c1::greater omentum}} connects from the <u>stomach</u> to the <u>transverse colon</u>	"<img src=""8c913f5e629520fcd0bb4eb4db8b2088.webp"">"			"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	c526219d-1c20-4012-a3d0-1dc274def44a	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The {{c1::peritoneum}} is a thin membrane consisting of a single layer of mesothelial cells that are supported by subserosal fat cells, lymphatic cells, and white blood cells.	"<img src=""8c913f5e629520fcd0bb4eb4db8b2088.webp"">"			"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	7fabce16-4048-4f2c-b167-b5e998a5d348	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The <b>{{c1::visceral}} peritoneum</b> lines the <u>surface of organs</u>,<br>while the <b>{{c1::parietal}} peritoneum</b> lines the <u>outer walls</u> of the peritoneal cavity.				"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	6ec2defc-c1c5-4eb8-9e01-976dd65692d3	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The most <u>dependent</u> portion of the peritoneal cavity <i>(both supine and upright)</i> is the {{c1::retro-uterine space (pouch of Douglas)::space}} in women and the {{c1::retrovesical space::space}} in men.				"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	9dd76295-dea6-4800-8b15-a211b1bb9279	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
There are {{c1::three::number}} true mesenteries, each of which supply a portion of the bowel and connect to the posterior abdominal wall.<br><br>Each mesentery consists of a network of blood vessels and&nbsp; lymphatics, sandwiched between layers of peritoneum.	"<img src=""07edc3fad20deaf880c2b7c554a0f98a.webp"">"			"<img src=""4a1311c8edf51a585b326cb3b07712e6.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	b2fe54a5-946a-4554-aac4-f4f6c9b10e38	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0222 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The <u>three true mesenteries</u> are:<br><br><ol><li>{{c1::<b>Small bowel mesentery</b>}}: Supplies both the jejunum and ileum. Oriented obliquely from the ligament of Treitz in the left upper quadrant to the ileocecal junction in the right lower quadrant. </li><li>{{c2::<b>Transverse mesocolon</b>}}<b>:</b> Mesentery to the transverse colon, connecting the posterior transverse colon to the posterior abdominal wall</li><li>{{c3::<b>Sigmoid mesentery</b>}}: Mesentery to the sigmoid colon.</li></ol>	"<img src=""07b92710ec8b12c7aa0f6904285668d3.webp"">"			"<img src=""9eae50b20af78d1aac980a04568e34b5.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	d46f2e22-0454-48ed-a1c3-e386ed5d3fdb	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0223 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
The <b>transverse mesocolon</b> divides the peritoneal cavity into {{c1::<u>supra-mesocolic</u>}} and {{c1::<u>infra-mesocolic</u>}}&nbsp;compartments,<br>the latter of which is divided into <u>right</u> and <u>left infracolic recesses</u> by the {{c2::<b>root of the small bowel mesentery</b>::structure}}. <b>Peritoneal fluid</b> preferentially travels from the pelvis into the upper abdomen via the paracolic gutters <i>(right &gt; left)</i> and pools in dependent recesses including:<br><br><ul><li>The <u>retrouterine</u> <i>(female)</i> / <u>retrovesical</u> <i>(male)</i> <u>recess</u></li><li>Along the <u>superior portion of the sigmoid mesocolon</u></li><li>The <u>ileocolic region</u> (root of the small bowel mesentery)</li><li>The <u>right paracolic gutter</u></li><li>In <u>Morrison’s pouch</u></li></ul><br><br>As a result, these regions are the <i>most prone</i> to involvement of {{c1::peritoneal and serosal metastases::complications}}.<br><br>Flow is limited anatomically in some locations like the falciform ligament on the right and the phrenicocolic ligament on the left.<br>				"<img src=""9eae50b20af78d1aac980a04568e34b5.webp"">"							Gastrointestinal Imaging: Mesentery, Peritoneum, and Omentum: Anatomy	0878081d-0176-4f3e-8f27-a7d783bf5b6e	"#Ankore::Textbooks::Core_Radiology::0223 AnkiHub_Subdeck::AnKore_for_ABR_Diagnostic_Radiology_Core_Exam::Core_Radiology::02_Gastrointestinal_Imaging::10_Mesentery,_peritoneum,_and_omentum Core_Radiology_2E"
